lang="bn">\xe0\xa6\x97\xe0\xa6\xa3\xe0\xa6\xaa\xe0\xa7\x8d\xe0\xa6\xb0\xe0\xa6\x9c\xe0\xa6\xbe\xe0\xa6\xa4\xe0\xa6\xa8\xe0\xa7\x8d\xe0\xa6\xa4\xe0\xa7\x8d\xe0\xa6\xb0\xe0\xa7\x80 \xe0\xa6\xac\xe0\xa6\xbe\xe0\xa6\x82\xe0\xa6\xb2\xe0\xa6\xbe\xe0\xa6\xa6\xe0\xa7\x87\xe0\xa6\xb6</span> <span title="Bengali transliteration" class="Unicode" style="white-space:normal; text-decoration: none"><a href="/wiki/Romanisation_of_Bengali#Romanisation_reference" title="Romanisation of Bengali"><i>Ga\xe1\xb9\x87apraj\xc4\x81tantr\xc4\xab B\xc4\x81\xe1\xb9\x83l\xc4\x81d\xc4\x93\xc5\x9ba</i></a></span>), is a country in <a href="/wiki/South_Asia" title="South Asia">South Asia</a>. It shares land borders with <a href="/wiki/India" title="India">India</a> and <a href="/wiki/Myanmar" title="Myanmar">Myanmar</a> (Burma). <a href="/wiki/Nepal" title="Nepal">Nepal</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bhutan" title="Bhutan">Bhutan</a> and <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">China</a> are located near Bangladesh but do not share a border with it. The country\'s maritime territory in the <a href="/wiki/Bay_of_Bengal" title="Bay of Bengal">Bay of Bengal</a> is roughly equal to the size of its land area.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup> Bangladesh is the world\'s <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_and_dependencies_by_population" title="List of countries and dependencies by population">eighth most populous country</a>. <a href="/wiki/Dhaka" title="Dhaka">Dhaka</a> is its capital and largest city, followed by <a href="/wiki/Chittagong" title="Chittagong">Chittagong</a>, which has the country\'s largest port.</p>\n<p>Bangladesh forms the largest and easternmost part of the <a href="/wiki/Bengal" title="Bengal">Bengal</a> region.<sup id="cite_ref-EyetsemitanGire2003_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EyetsemitanGire2003-11">[11]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Bangladeshis" title="Bangladeshis">Bangladeshis</a> include people from a range of ethnic groups and religions. <a href="/wiki/Bengalis" title="Bengalis">Bengalis</a>, who speak the official <a href="/wiki/Bengali_language" title="Bengali language">Bengali language</a>, make up 98% of the population.<sup id="cite_ref-bdlaws.minlaw.gov.bd_2-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bdlaws.minlaw.gov.bd-2">[2]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-.E0.A6.AC.E0.A6.BE.E0.A6.82.E0.A6.B2.E0.A6.BE.E0.A6.A6.E0.A7.87.E0.A6.B6.E0.A6.95.E0.A7.87_.E0.A6.9C.E0.A6.BE.E0.A6.A8.E0.A7.81.E0.A6.A8_3-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-.E0.A6.AC.E0.A6.BE.E0.A6.82.E0.A6.B2.E0.A6.BE.E0.A6.A6.E0.A7.87.E0.A6.B6.E0.A6.95.E0.A7.87_.E0.A6.9C.E0.A6.BE.E0.A6.A8.E0.A7.81.E0.A6.A8-3">[3]</a></sup> The politically dominant <a href="/wiki/Bengali_Muslims" title="Bengali Muslims">Bengali Muslims</a> make the nation the world\'s third largest <a href="/wiki/Islam_by_country" title="Islam by country">Muslim-majority country</a>. Most of Bangladesh is covered by the <a href="/wiki/Bengal_delta" class="mw-redirect" title="Bengal delta">Bengal delta</a>, the largest delta on Earth. The country has 700 rivers and 8,046&#160;km (5,000 miles) of inland waterways. <a href="/wiki/List_of_mountains_in_Bangladesh" class="mw-redirect" title="List of mountains in Bangladesh">Highlands</a> with evergreen forests are found in the northeastern and southeastern regions of the country. Bangladesh has many islands and a coral reef. The longest unbroken sea beach, <a href="/wiki/Cox%27s_Bazar_Beach" title="Cox\'s Bazar Beach">Cox\'s Bazar Beach</a> is located here. It is home to the <a href="/wiki/Sundarbans" title="Sundarbans">Sundarbans</a>, the largest mangrove forest in the world. The country\'s <a href="/wiki/Biodiversity" title="Biodiversity">biodiversity</a> includes a vast array of plant and wildlife, including endangered <a href="/wiki/Bengal_tiger" title="Bengal tiger">Bengal tigers</a>, the national animal.</p>\n<p>The Greeks and Romans identified the region as <a href="/wiki/Gangaridai" title="Gangaridai">Gangaridai</a>, a powerful kingdom of the historical <a href="/wiki/Subcontinent" class="mw-redirect" title="Subcontinent">subcontinent</a>, in the 3rd century BCE. Archaeological research has unearthed several ancient cities in Bangladesh, which enjoyed international trade links for millennia.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Bengal_Sultanate" title="Bengal Sultanate">Bengal Sultanate</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mughal_Bengal" class="mw-redirect" title="Mughal Bengal">Mughal Bengal</a> transformed the region into a cosmopolitan <a href="/wiki/Islamic" class="mw-redirect" title="Islamic">Islamic</a> imperial power between the 14th and 18th centuries. The region was home to many principalities that made use of their inland <a href="/wiki/Naval" class="mw-redirect" title="Naval">naval</a> prowess.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-en.banglapedia.org_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-en.banglapedia.org-14">[14]</a></sup> It was also a notable center of the global <a href="/wiki/Muslin_trade_in_Bengal" title="Muslin trade in Bengal">muslin</a> and silk trade. As part of <a href="/wiki/British_India" class="mw-redirect" title="British India">British India</a>, the region was influenced by the <a href="/wiki/Bengali_renaissance" title="Bengali renaissance">Bengali renaissance</a> and played an important role in <a href="/wiki/Decolonization" title="Decolonization">anti-colonial movements</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Partition_of_British_India" class="mw-redirect" title="Partition of British India">Partition of British India</a> made East Bengal a part of the <a href="/wiki/Dominion_of_Pakistan" title="Dominion of Pakistan">Dominion of Pakistan</a>; and renamed it as <a href="/wiki/East_Pakistan" title="East Pakistan">East Pakistan</a>. The region witnessed the <a href="/wiki/Bengali_Language_Movement" class="mw-redirect" title="Bengali Language Movement">Bengali Language Movement</a> in 1952 and the <a href="/wiki/Bangladesh_Liberation_War" title="Bangladesh Liberation War">Bangladesh Liberation War</a> in 1971. After independence was achieved, a <a href="/wiki/Parliamentary_republic" title="Parliamentary republic">parliamentary republic</a> was established. A <a href="/wiki/Presidential_government" class="mw-redirect" title="Presidential government">presidential government</a> was in place between 1975 and 1990, followed by a return to parliamentary democracy. The country continues to face challenges in the areas of <a href="/wiki/Poverty_in_Bangladesh" title="Poverty in Bangladesh">poverty</a>, <a href="/wiki/Education_in_Bangladesh" title="Education in Bangladesh">education</a>, <a href="/wiki/Health_in_Bangladesh" title="Health in Bangladesh">healthcare</a> and <a href="/wiki/Corruption_in_Bangladesh" title="Corruption in Bangladesh">corruption</a>.</p>\n<p>Bangladesh is a <a href="/wiki/Middle_power" title="Middle power">middle power</a> and a <a href="/wiki/Developing_nation" class="mw-redirect" title="Developing nation">developing nation</a>. Listed as one of the <a href="/wiki/Next_Eleven" title="Next Eleven">Next Eleven</a>, its economy ranks <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_nominal_GDP" class="mw-redirect" title="List of countries by nominal GDP">46th</a> in terms of nominal <a href="/wiki/Gross_domestic_product" title="Gross domestic product">gross domestic product</a> (GDP) and <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_GDP_(PPP)" title="List of countries by GDP (PPP)">29th</a> in terms of <a href="/wiki/Purchasing_power_parity" title="Purchasing power parity">purchasing power parity</a> (PPP). It is one of the <a href="/wiki/Bangladesh_textile_industry" class="mw-redirect" title="Bangladesh textile industry">largest textile exporters</a> in the world. Its major trading partners are the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a>, the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a>, China, India, <a href="/wiki/Japan" title="Japan">Japan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Malaysia" title="Malaysia">Malaysia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Singapore" title="Singapore">Singapore</a>. With its strategically vital location between Southern, Eastern and Southeast Asia, Bangladesh is an important promoter of regional connectivity and cooperation. It is a founding member of <a href="/wiki/SAARC" class="mw-redirect" title="SAARC">SAARC</a>, <a href="/wiki/BIMSTEC" class="mw-redirect" title="BIMSTEC">BIMSTEC</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Bangladesh-China-India-Myanmar_Forum_for_Regional_Cooperation" class="mw-redirect" title="Bangladesh-China-India-Myanmar Forum for Regional Cooperation">Bangladesh-China-India-Myanmar Forum for Regional Cooperation</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Bangladesh_Bhutan_India_Nepal" class="mw-redirect" title="Bangladesh Bhutan India Nepal">Bangladesh Bhutan India Nepal</a> Initiative. It is also a member of the <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_Nations" title="Commonwealth of Nations">Commonwealth of Nations</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Developing_8_Countries" class="mw-redirect" title="Developing 8 Countries">Developing 8 Countries</a>, the <a href="/wiki/OIC" class="mw-redirect" title="OIC">OIC</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Non_Aligned_Movement" class="mw-redirect" title="Non Aligned Movement">Non Aligned Movement</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Group_of_77" title="Group of 77">Group of 77</a> and the <a href="/wiki/World_Trade_Organization" title="World Trade Organization">World Trade Organization</a>. Bangladesh is one of the largest contributors to <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_peacekeeping" title="United Nations peacekeeping">United Nations peacekeeping</a> forces.</p>\n<p></p>\n<div id="toc" Bangladesh</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-38"><a href="#Architecture"><span class="tocnumber">7.4</span> <span class="toctext">Architecture</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 class="toctext">References</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-51"><a href="#Cited_sources"><span class="tocnumber">10</span> <span class="toctext">Cited sources</span></a></li>\n<li
