text-align:right">\n<center>1,015</center>\n</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td>Rangpur</td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Rangpur_City" title="Rangpur City">Rangpur</a></td>\n<td style="text-align:right;">\n<center>25 January 2010</center>\n</td>\n<td style="text-align:right;">\n<center>16,317</center>\n</td>\n<td style="text-align:right;">\n<center>15,787,758</center>\n</td>\n<td style="text-align:right;">\n<center>960</center>\n</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td style="background:#f0f0f0">Sylhet</td>\n<td style="background:#f0f0f0"><a href="/wiki/Sylhet" title="Sylhet">Sylhet</a></td>\n<td style="background:#f0f0f0">\n<center>1 August 1995</center>\n</td>\n<td style="background:#f0f0f0; text-align:right">\n<center>12,596</center>\n</td>\n<td style="background:#f0f0f0; text-align:right">\n<center>9,910,219</center>\n</td>\n<td style="background:#f0f0f0; text-align:right">\n<center>780</center>\n</td>\n</tr>\n</table>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Climate_of_Bangladesh" class="mw-redirect" title="Climate of Bangladesh">Climate of Bangladesh</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Jamuna_River_Bogra,_Bangladesh_01.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/Jamuna_River_Bogra%2C_Bangladesh_01.jpg/220px-Jamuna_River_Bogra%2C_Bangladesh_01.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/Jamuna_River_Bogra%2C_Bangladesh_01.jpg/330px-Jamuna_River_Bogra%2C_Bangladesh_01.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/Jamuna_River_Bogra%2C_Bangladesh_01.jpg/440px-Jamuna_River_Bogra%2C_Bangladesh_01.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3264" data-file-height="2448" /></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Jamuna_River_Bogra,_Bangladesh_01.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\n<a href="/wiki/Climate_change" title="Climate change">Climate change</a> is causing increasing <a href="/wiki/River_erosion" class="mw-redirect" title="River erosion">river erosion</a> in Bangladesh, threatening an estimated 20 million people</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>Straddling the <a href="/wiki/Tropic_of_Cancer" title="Tropic of Cancer">Tropic of Cancer</a>, Bangladesh\'s climate is tropical with a mild winter from October to March, and a hot, humid summer from March to June. The country has never recorded an air temperature below 0&#160;\xc2\xb0C (32&#160;\xc2\xb0F), with a record low of 1.1&#160;\xc2\xb0C (34.0&#160;\xc2\xb0F) in the north west city of <a href="/wiki/Dinajpur" title="Dinajpur">Dinajpur</a> on 3 February 1905.<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">[98]</a></sup> A warm and humid monsoon season lasts from June to October and supplies most of the country\'s rainfall.</p>\n<p>Natural calamities, such as <a href="/wiki/Floods_in_Bangladesh" title="Floods in Bangladesh">floods</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tropical_cyclone" title="Tropical cyclone">tropical cyclones</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tornado" title="Tornado">tornadoes</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Tidal_bore" title="Tidal bore">tidal bores</a> occur almost every year,<sup id="cite_ref-NatDis_99-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NatDis-99">[99]</a></sup> combined with the effects of <a href="/wiki/Deforestation" title="Deforestation">deforestation</a>, <a href="/wiki/Soils_retrogression_and_degradation" class="mw-redirect" title="Soils retrogression and degradation">soil degradation</a> and <a href="/wiki/Erosion" title="Erosion">erosion</a>. The <a href="/wiki/List_of_Bangladesh_tropical_cyclones" title="List of Bangladesh tropical cyclones">cyclones</a> of 1970 and 1991 were particularly devastating, the <a href="/wiki/1991_Bangladesh_cyclone" title="1991 Bangladesh cyclone">latter</a> killing some 140,000 people.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">[100]</a></sup></p>\n<p>In September 1998, Bangladesh saw <a href="/wiki/1998_Bangladesh_floods" class="mw-redirect" title="1998 Bangladesh floods">the most severe flooding</a> in modern world history. As the Brahmaputra, the Ganges and <a href="/wiki/Meghna" class="mw-redirect" title="Meghna">Meghna</a> spilt over and swallowed 300,000 houses, 9,700&#160;km (6,000&#160;mi) of road and 2,700&#160;km (1,700&#160;mi) of embankment, 1,000&#160;people were killed and 30&#160;million more made homeless, 135,000 cattle killed, 50&#160;km<sup>2</sup> (19&#160;sq&#160;mi) of land destroyed and 11,000&#160;km (6,800&#160;mi) of roads damaged or destroyed. Effectively, two-thirds of the country was underwater. The severity of the flooding was attributed to unusually high <a href="/wiki/Monsoon" title="Monsoon">monsoon</a> rains, the shedding off of equally unusually large amounts of melt water from the <a href="/wiki/Himalayas" title="Himalayas">Himalayas</a>, and the widespread cutting down of trees (that would have intercepted rain water) for firewood or animal husbandry.<sup id="cite_ref-EWG_101-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EWG-101">[101]</a></sup></p>\n<p>Bangladesh is now widely recognised to be one of the countries most vulnerable to <a href="/wiki/Climate_change_in_Bangladesh" title="Climate change in Bangladesh">climate change</a>. Natural hazards that come from increased rainfall, rising sea levels, and tropical cyclones are expected to increase as climate changes, each seriously affecting agriculture, water and food security, human health and shelter.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">[102]</a></sup> It is believed that in the coming decades the rising sea level alone will create more than 20 million<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">[103]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Climate_refugee" class="mw-redirect" title="Climate refugee">climate refugees</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">[104]</a></sup></p>\n<p>Bangladesh is prone to <a href="/wiki/Flood" title="Flood">floods</a>, tornadoes and <a href="/wiki/Cyclone" title="Cyclone">cyclones</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">[105]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">[106]</a></sup> Also, there is evidence that earthquakes pose a threat to the country, and that tectonics have caused rivers to shift course suddenly and dramatically. It has also been shown that rainy-season flooding in Bangladesh, on the world\'s largest river delta, can push the underlying crust down by as much as 6&#160;centimetres, and possibly perturb faults.<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">[107]</a></sup></p>\n<p>Bangladeshi water is frequently contaminated with <a href="/wiki/Arsenic" title="Arsenic">arsenic</a> because of the high arsenic content of the soil\xe2\x80\x94up to 77 million people are <a href="/wiki/Arsenic_contamination_of_groundwater" title="Arsenic contamination of groundwater">exposed to toxic arsenic</a> from drinking water.<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">[108]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">[109]</a></sup></p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Biodiversity">Biodiversity</span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Wildlife_of_Bangladesh" title="Wildlife of Bangladesh">Wildlife of Bangladesh</a> and <a href="/wiki/Fauna_of_Bangladesh" title="Fauna of Bangladesh">Fauna of Bangladesh</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Tiger_Sundarbans_Tiger_Reserve_22.07.2015.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/Tiger_Sundarbans_Tiger_Reserve_22.07.2015.jpg/300px-Tiger_Sundarbans_Tiger_Reserve_22.07.2015.jpg" width="300" height="200" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/Tiger_Sundarbans_Tiger_Reserve_22.07.2015.jpg/450px-Tiger_Sundarbans_Tiger_Reserve_22.07.2015.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/Tiger_Sundarbans_Tiger_Reserve_22.07.2015.jpg/600px-Tiger_Sundarbans_Tiger_Reserve_22.07.2015.jpg 2x" data-file-width="900" data-file-height="600" /></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Tiger_Sundarbans_Tiger_Reserve_22.07.2015.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nA <a href="/wiki/Bengal_tiger" title="Bengal tiger">Bengal tiger</a>, the national animal, in the Sunderbans</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Axishirsche_in_den_Sundarbans.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/Axishirsche_in_den_Sundarbans.JPG/300px-Axishirsche_in_den_Sundarbans.JPG" width="300" height="189" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/Axishirsche_in_den_Sundarbans.JPG/450px-Axishirsche_in_den_Sundarbans.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/Axishirsche_in_den_Sundarbans.JPG/600px-Axishirsche_in_den_Sundarbans.JPG 2x" data-file-width="4142" data-file-height="2611" /></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Axishirsche_in_den_Sundarbans.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\n<a href="/wiki/Axis_deer" class="mw-redirect" title="Axis deer">Axis deer</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Sunderbans" class="mw-redirect" title="Sunderbans">Sunderbans</a></div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>Bangladesh ratified the Rio <a href="/wiki/Convention_on_Biological_Diversity" title="Convention on Biological Diversity">Convention on Biological Diversity</a> on 3 May 1994.<sup id="cite_ref-cbd.int_110-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cbd.int-110">[110]</a></sup> As of 2014<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Bangladesh&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, the country was set to revise its <a href="/wiki/Biodiversity_action_plan" title="Biodiversity action plan">National Biodiversity Strategy and Action Plan</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-cbd.int_110-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cbd.int-110">[110]</a></sup></p>\n<p>Bangladesh is located in the <a href="/wiki/Indomalaya_ecozone" class="mw-redirect" title="Indomalaya ecozone">Indomalaya ecozone</a>. Its ecology includes a long sea coastline, numerous <a href="/wiki/List_of_rivers_in_Bangladesh" class="mw-redirect" title="List of rivers in Bangladesh">rivers and tributaries</a>, lakes, <a href="/wiki/Wetland" title="Wetland">wetlands</a>, evergreen forests, semi evergreen forests, hill forests, moist <a href="/wiki/Deciduous_forest" class="mw-redirect" title="Deciduous forest">deciduous forests</a>, freshwater swamp forests and flat land with tall grass. The Bangladesh Plain is famous for its fertile <a href="/wiki/Alluvial" class="mw-redirect" title="Alluvial">alluvial</a> soil which supports extensive cultivation. The country is dominated by lush vegetation, with villages often buried in groves of <a href="/wiki/Mango" title="Mango">mango</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jackfruit" title="Jackfruit">jackfruit</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bamboo" title="Bamboo">bamboo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Betel_nut" class="mw-redirect" title="Betel nut">betel nut</a>, <a href="/wiki/Coconut" title="Coconut">coconut</a> and <a href="/wiki/Date_palm" title="Date palm">date palm</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-global.britannica.com_111-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-global.britannica.com-111">[111]</a></sup> The country has up to 6000 species of plant life, including 5000 flowering plants.<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">[112]</a></sup> Water bodies and wetland systems provide a habitat for many aquatic plants. <a href="/wiki/Nymphaeaceae" title="Nymphaeaceae">Water lilies</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nelumbo_nucifera" title="Nelumbo nucifera">lotuses</a> grow vividly during the monsoon season. The country has <a href="/wiki/List_of_protected_areas_of_Bangladesh" title="List of protected areas of Bangladesh">50 wildlife sanctuaries</a>.</p>\n<p>Bangladesh is home to much of the <a href="/wiki/Sundarbans" title="Sundarbans">Sundarbans</a>, the world\'s largest <a href="/wiki/Mangrove_forest" class="mw-redirect" title="Mangrove forest">mangrove forest</a>, covering an area of 6,000&#160;km<sup>2</sup> in the southwest littoral region. It is divided into three protected sanctuaries\xe2\x80\x93the <a href="/wiki/Sundarbans_South_Wildlife_Sanctuary" title="Sundarbans South Wildlife Sanctuary">South</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sundarbans_East_Wildlife_Sanctuary" title="Sundarbans East Wildlife Sanctuary">East</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sundarbans_West_Wildlife_Sanctuary" title="Sundarbans West Wildlife Sanctuary">West</a> zones. The forest is a UNESCO World Heritage Site. The northeastern Sylhet region is home to haor wetlands, which is a unique ecosystem. It also includes <a href="/wiki/Tropical_and_subtropical_coniferous_forests" title="Tropical and subtropical coniferous forests">tropical and subtropical coniferous forests</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Freshwater_swamp_forest" title="Freshwater swamp forest">freshwater swamp forest</a> and mixed deciduous forests. The southeastern <a href="/wiki/Chittagong_Division" title="Chittagong Division">Chittagong region</a> covers evergreen and semi evergreen hilly jungles. Central Bangladesh includes the plainland Sal forest running along the districts of Gazipur, <a href="/wiki/Tangail" title="Tangail">Tangail</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mymensingh" title="Mymensingh">Mymensingh</a>. <a href="/wiki/St._Martin%27s_Island" title="St. Martin\'s Island">St. Martin\'s Island</a> is the only <a href="/wiki/Coral_reef" title="Coral reef">coral reef</a> in the country.</p>\n<p>Bangladesh has an abundance of <a href="/wiki/Wildlife_in_Bangladesh" class="mw-redirect" title="Wildlife in Bangladesh">wildlife</a> in its forests, marshes, woodlands and hills.<sup id="cite_ref-global.britannica.com_111-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-global.britannica.com-111">[111]</a></sup> The vast majority of animals dwell within a habitat of 150,000&#160;km<sup>2</sup>.<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">[113]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Bengal_tiger" title="Bengal tiger">Bengal tiger</a>, <a href="/wiki/Clouded_leopard" title="Clouded leopard">clouded leopard</a>, <a href="/wiki/Saltwater_crocodile" title="Saltwater crocodile">saltwater crocodile</a>, <a href="/wiki/Black_panther" title="Black panther">black panther</a> and <a href="/wiki/Fishing_cat" title="Fishing cat">fishing cat</a> are among the chief predators in the Sundarbans.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">[114]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ibtimes.co.uk_115-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ibtimes.co.uk-115">[115]</a></sup> Northern and eastern Bangladesh is home to the <a href="/wiki/Asian_elephant" title="Asian elephant">Asian elephant</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hoolock_gibbon" title="Hoolock gibbon">hoolock gibbon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Asian_black_bear" title="Asian black bear">Asian black bear</a> and <a href="/wiki/Oriental_pied_hornbill" title="Oriental pied hornbill">oriental pied hornbill</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-bearprojectbd.weebly.com_116-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bearprojectbd.weebly.com-116">[116]</a></sup></p>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Chital" title="Chital">Chital</a> deer are widely seen in southwestern woodlands. Other animals include the <a href="/wiki/Black_giant_squirrel" title="Black giant squirrel">black giant squirrel</a>, <a href="/wiki/Capped_langur" title="Capped langur">capped langur</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bengal_fox" title="Bengal fox">Bengal fox</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sambar_deer" title="Sambar deer">sambar deer</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jungle_cat" title="Jungle cat">jungle cat</a>, <a href="/wiki/King_cobra" title="King cobra">king cobra</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wild_boar" title="Wild boar">wild boar</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mongoose" title="Mongoose">mongooses</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pangolin" title="Pangolin">pangolins</a>, <a href="/wiki/Python_(genus)" title="Python (genus)">pythons</a> and <a href="/wiki/Asian_water_monitor" title="Asian water monitor">water monitors</a>. Bangladesh has one of the largest population of <a href="/wiki/Irrawaddy_dolphins" class="mw-redirect" title="Irrawaddy dolphins">Irrawaddy dolphins</a> and <a href="/wiki/South_Asian_river_dolphin" title="South Asian river dolphin">Ganges dolphins</a>. A 2009 census found 6,000 Irrawaddy dolphins inhabiting the littoral rivers of Bangladesh.<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">[117]</a></sup> The country has numerous species of <a href="/wiki/Amphibian" title="Amphibian">amphibians</a> (53), reptiles (139), <a href="/wiki/Marine_reptile" title="Marine reptile">marine reptiles</a> (19) and <a href="/wiki/Marine_mammal" title="Marine mammal">marine mammals</a> (5). It also has <a href="/wiki/List_of_birds_of_Bangladesh" title="List of birds of Bangladesh">628 species of birds</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">[118]</a></sup></p>\n<p>Several animals became extinct in Bangladesh during the last century, including the one horned and two horned <a href="/wiki/Rhinoceros" title="Rhinoceros">rhinoceros</a> and common <a href="/wiki/Peafowl" title="Peafowl">peafowl</a>. The human population is concentrated in urban areas, hence limiting deforestation to a certain extent. Rapid urban growth has threatened natural habitats. Though many areas are protected under law, a large portion of Bangladeshi wildlife is threatened by this growth. The <a href="/wiki/Bangladesh_Environment_Conservation_Act" title="Bangladesh Environment Conservation Act">Bangladesh Environment Conservation Act</a> was enacted in 1995. The government has designated several regions as <a href="/wiki/Ecologically_Critical_Area" title="Ecologically Critical Area">Ecologically Critical Areas</a>, including wetlands, forests and rivers. The <a href="/wiki/Sundarbans_tiger_project" class="mw-redirect" title="Sundarbans tiger project">Sundarbans Tiger Project</a> and the Bangladesh Bear Project are among the key initiatives to strengthen conservation.<sup id="cite_ref-bearprojectbd.weebly.com_116-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bearprojectbd.weebly.com-116">[116]</a></sup></p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Politics">Politics</span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_Bangladesh" title="Politics of Bangladesh">Politics of Bangladesh</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bangabhaban.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Aerial view of a large, low building surrounded by green space" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/Bangabhaban.jpg/220px-Bangabhaban.jpg" width="220" height="130" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/Bangabhaban.jpg/330px-Bangabhaban.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/Bangabhaban.jpg/440px-Bangabhaban.jpg 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="472" /></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bangabhaban.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nBangabhaban, the residence of the president of Bangladesh</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Bangladesh" title="Constitution of Bangladesh">Constitution of Bangladesh</a> established a <a href="/wiki/Unitary_state" title="Unitary state">unitary</a>, <a href="/wiki/Westminster" title="Westminster">Westminster</a>-style <a href="/wiki/Parliamentary_republic" title="Parliamentary republic">parliamentary republic</a> with <a href="/wiki/Universal_suffrage" title="Universal suffrage">universal suffrage</a>. A <a href="/wiki/Member_of_parliament" title="Member of parliament">member of parliament</a> supported by a parliamentary majority (usually the chair of the largest party) is the <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Bangladesh" title="Prime Minister of Bangladesh">Prime Minister</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Government_of_Bangladesh" title="Government of Bangladesh">head of government</a> and of the <a href="/wiki/Cabinet_of_Bangladesh" title="Cabinet of Bangladesh">cabinet</a>. Bangladesh is governed by a 350-member parliament, known as the <a href="/wiki/Jatiyo_Sangshad" class="mw-redirect" title="Jatiyo Sangshad">Jatiyo Sangshad</a>. Three hundred of its members are elected on a <a href="/wiki/First_past_the_post" class="mw-redirect" title="First past the post">first past the post</a> basis, and 50 seats are reserved for female nominees by political parties. Although parliamentary <a href="/wiki/Elections_in_Bangladesh" title="Elections in Bangladesh">elections</a> are scheduled every five years, they have often been delayed by political crises, emergency rule or <a href="/wiki/Military_coups_in_Bangladesh" title="Military coups in Bangladesh">martial law</a>. The <a href="/wiki/President_of_Bangladesh" title="President of Bangladesh">President of Bangladesh</a> is the <a href="/wiki/Head_of_state" title="Head of state">head of state</a>. From 1975 to 1990 the presidency had executive powers, but it has been reduced to a largely-ceremonial role by the <a href="/wiki/Amendments_to_the_Constitution_of_Bangladesh" title="Amendments to the Constitution of Bangladesh">Twelfth Amendment</a> to the constitution.</p>\n<p>In 2011, the <a href="/wiki/Amendments_to_the_Constitution_of_Bangladesh" title="Amendments to the Constitution of Bangladesh">Fifteenth Amendment</a> mandated the "highest punishment" for <a href="/wiki/Usurper" title="Usurper">usurpers</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">[119]</a></sup> The amendment was controversial for abolishing the <a href="/wiki/Caretaker_government_of_Bangladesh" title="Caretaker government of Bangladesh">caretaker-government system</a>, which had been a neutral administration during election periods since the 1990s.<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">[120]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Bangladesh_general_election,_2014" class="mw-redirect" title="Bangladesh general election, 2014">2014 national election</a> was boycotted by the largest opposition party, which argued that a free election could not be held without a neutral interim government. The Jatiyo Sangshad is restrained from holding <a href="/wiki/No-confidence" class="mw-redirect" title="No-confidence">no-confidence</a> motions, <a href="/wiki/Crossing_the_floor" title="Crossing the floor">floor crossing</a> and <a href="/wiki/Free_vote" class="mw-redirect" title="Free vote">free votes</a> by <a href="/wiki/Article_70_of_the_Constitution_of_Bangladesh" title="Article 70 of the Constitution of Bangladesh">Article 70 of the constitution</a>. <a href="/wiki/Human_rights_in_Bangladesh" title="Human rights in Bangladesh">Human-rights</a> violations have increased due to the growing power of security forces\xe2\x80\x94particularly the <a href="/wiki/Rapid_Action_Battalion" title="Rapid Action Battalion">Rapid Action Battalion</a>, which is accused of arbitrary arrests, summary executions and <a href="/wiki/Forced_disappearance_in_Bangladesh" title="Forced disappearance in Bangladesh">forced disappearances</a>.</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Legal_system">Legal system</span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Laws_in_Bangladesh" title="Laws in Bangladesh">Laws in Bangladesh</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tleft">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bangladesh_Supreme_Court.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Long, white, domed building" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Bangladesh_Supreme_Court.jpg/220px-Bangladesh_Supreme_Court.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Bangladesh_Supreme_Court.jpg/330px-Bangladesh_Supreme_Court.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Bangladesh_Supreme_Court.jpg/440px-Bangladesh_Supreme_Court.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1023" data-file-height="767" /></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bangladesh_Supreme_Court.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nSupreme Court of Bangladesh</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>Bangladesh\'s legal system is based on <a href="/wiki/Common_law" title="Common law">common law</a>, and its principal source of laws are <a href="/wiki/Acts_of_Parliament" class="mw-redirect" title="Acts of Parliament">acts of Parliament</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">[121]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Bangladesh_Code" title="Bangladesh Code">Bangladesh Code</a> includes a list of all laws in force in the country. The code begins in 1836, and most of its listed laws were crafted under the <a href="/wiki/British_Raj" title="British Raj">British Raj</a> by the <a href="/wiki/Bengal_Legislative_Council" title="Bengal Legislative Council">Bengal Legislative Council</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Bengal_Legislative_Assembly" title="Bengal Legislative Assembly">Bengal Legislative Assembly</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Bengal_and_Assam_Legislative_Council" class="mw-redirect" title="Eastern Bengal and Assam Legislative Council">Eastern Bengal and Assam Legislative Council</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Imperial_Legislative_Council" title="Imperial Legislative Council">Imperial Legislative Council</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Parliament_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Parliament of the United Kingdom">Parliament of the United Kingdom</a>; one example is the <a href="/wiki/The_Penal_Code,_1860_(Bangladesh)" title="The Penal Code, 1860 (Bangladesh)">1860 Penal Code</a>. From 1947 to 1971, laws were enacted by Pakistan\'s <a href="/wiki/National_Assembly_of_Pakistan" title="National Assembly of Pakistan">national assembly</a> and the <a href="/wiki/East_Pakistan_Provincial_Assembly" title="East Pakistan Provincial Assembly">East Pakistani legislature</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Constituent_Assembly_of_Bangladesh" title="Constituent Assembly of Bangladesh">Constituent Assembly of Bangladesh</a> was the country\'s provisional parliament until 1973, when the first elected Jatiyo Sangshad was sworn in. Although most of Bangladesh\'s laws were compiled in <a href="/wiki/English_language" title="English language">English</a>, after a 1987 government directive laws are now primarily written in <a href="/wiki/Bengali_language" title="Bengali language">Bengali</a>. Marriage, divorce and inheritance are governed by <a href="/wiki/Islamic_law" class="mw-redirect" title="Islamic law">Islamic</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hindu_law" title="Hindu law">Hindu</a> and Christian <a href="/wiki/Family_law" title="Family law">family law</a>. The judiciary is often influenced by legal developments in the <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_Nations" title="Commonwealth of Nations">Commonwealth of Nations</a>, such as the <a href="/wiki/Legitimate_expectation" title="Legitimate expectation">doctrine of legitimate expectation</a>.</p>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Court_of_Bangladesh" title="Supreme Court of Bangladesh">Supreme Court of Bangladesh</a>, including its <a href="/wiki/High_Court_Division" title="High Court Division">High Court</a> and Appellate Divisions, is the high court of the land. The head of the judiciary is the <a href="/wiki/Chief_Justice_of_Bangladesh" title="Chief Justice of Bangladesh">Chief Justice of Bangladesh</a>, who sits on the Supreme Court. The courts have wide latitude in <a href="/wiki/Judicial_review_in_Bangladesh" title="Judicial review in Bangladesh">judicial review</a>, and judicial <a href="/wiki/Precedent" title="Precedent">precedent</a> is supported by the Article 111 of the constitution. The <a href="/wiki/Judiciary_of_Bangladesh" title="Judiciary of Bangladesh">judiciary</a> includes district and metropolitan courts, which are divided into civil and criminal courts. Due to a shortage of judges, the judiciary has a large backlog. The <a href="/wiki/Bangladesh_Judicial_Service_Commission" title="Bangladesh Judicial Service Commission">Bangladesh Judicial Service Commission</a> is an independent body responsible for judicial appointments, salaries and discipline.</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Military">Military</span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Bangladesh_Armed_Forces" title="Bangladesh Armed Forces">Bangladesh Armed Forces</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:BangladeshMilitaryUN_PeacekeepingForce.jpg" class="image"><img alt="World map, indicating where the Bangladeshi UN peacekeeping force is stationed" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a6/BangladeshMilitaryUN_PeacekeepingForce.jpg/220px-BangladeshMilitaryUN_PeacekeepingForce.jpg" width="220" height="138" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a6/BangladeshMilitaryUN_PeacekeepingForce.jpg/330px-BangladeshMilitaryUN_PeacekeepingForce.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a6/BangladeshMilitaryUN_PeacekeepingForce.jpg/440px-BangladeshMilitaryUN_PeacekeepingForce.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1178" data-file-height="738" /></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:BangladeshMilitaryUN_PeacekeepingForce.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nMap of <a href="/wiki/Bangladesh_UN_Peacekeeping_Force" title="Bangladesh UN Peacekeeping Force">Bangladesh UN Peacekeeping Force</a> deployments</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>The Bangladesh Armed Forces have inherited the institutional framework of the <a href="/wiki/British_military" class="mw-redirect" title="British military">British military</a> and the <a href="/wiki/British_Indian_Army" title="British Indian Army">British Indian Army</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">[122]</a></sup> It was formed in 1971 from the military regiments of East Pakistan. In 2012 the <a href="/wiki/Bangladesh_Army" title="Bangladesh Army">army</a> strength was around 300,000, including reservists,<sup id="cite_ref-Al_Jazeera_123-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Al_Jazeera-123">[123]</a></sup> the Air Force (22,000) and the Navy (24,000).<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">[124]</a></sup> In addition to traditional defence roles, the military has supported civil authorities in disaster relief and provided internal security during periods of political unrest. For many years, Bangladesh has been the world\'s largest contributor to <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_peacekeeping" title="United Nations peacekeeping">UN peacekeeping forces</a>. In February 2015, the country made major deployments to <a href="/wiki/Cote_d%27Ivoire" class="mw-redirect" title="Cote d\'Ivoire">C\xc3\xb4te d\'Ivoire</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cyprus" title="Cyprus">Cyprus</a>, <a href="/wiki/Darfur" title="Darfur">Darfur</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Republic_of_Congo" class="mw-redirect" title="Democratic Republic of Congo">Democratic Republic of Congo</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Golan_Heights" title="Golan Heights">Golan Heights</a>, <a href="/wiki/Haiti" title="Haiti">Haiti</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lebanon" title="Lebanon">Lebanon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Liberia" title="Liberia">Liberia</a> and <a href="/wiki/South_Sudan" title="South Sudan">South Sudan</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">[125]</a></sup></p>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Bangladesh_Navy" title="Bangladesh Navy">Bangladesh Navy</a> has the third-largest fleet (after India and Thailand) of <a href="/wiki/Countries_dependent_on_the_Bay_of_Bengal" title="Countries dependent on the Bay of Bengal">countries dependent on the Bay of Bengal</a>, including <a href="/wiki/Guided-missile_frigate" class="mw-redirect" title="Guided-missile frigate">guided-missile frigates</a>, <a href="/wiki/Submarine" title="Submarine">submarines</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cutter_(boat)" title="Cutter (boat)">cutters</a> and aircraft. The <a href="/wiki/Bangladesh_Air_Force" title="Bangladesh Air Force">Bangladesh Air Force</a> is equipped with several Russian multi-role fighter jets. Bangladesh cooperates defensively with the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Armed_Forces" title="United States Armed Forces">United States Armed Forces</a>, participating in the <a href="/wiki/Cooperation_Afloat_Readiness_and_Training" title="Cooperation Afloat Readiness and Training">Cooperation Afloat Readiness and Training</a> (CARAT) exercises. Ties between the Bangladeshi and the <a href="/wiki/Indian_military" class="mw-redirect" title="Indian military">Indian military</a> have increased, with high-level visits by the military chiefs of both countries.<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">[126]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">[127]</a></sup> Eighty percent of Bangladesh\'s military equipment comes from China.<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">[128]</a></sup></p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Foreign_relations">Foreign relations</span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_Bangladesh" title="Foreign relations of Bangladesh">Foreign relations of Bangladesh</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a href="/wiki/File:1st_Saarc_summit.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Leaders seated at a dais" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/b4/1st_Saarc_summit.jpg/300px-1st_Saarc_summit.jpg" width="300" height="121" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/b4/1st_Saarc_summit.jpg/450px-1st_Saarc_summit.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/b4/1st_Saarc_summit.jpg/600px-1st_Saarc_summit.jpg 2x" data-file-width="619" data-file-height="250" /></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:1st_Saarc_summit.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nFirst South Asian Association for Regional Cooperation (SAARC) meeting in 1985 in Dhaka (<i>l-r, top row</i>: the presidents of <a href="/wiki/Pakistan" title="Pakistan">Pakistan</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Maldives" title="Maldives">Maldives</a>, the king of <a href="/wiki/Bhutan" title="Bhutan">Bhutan</a>, the president of Bangladesh, the prime minister of <a href="/wiki/India" title="India">India</a>, the king of <a href="/wiki/Nepal" title="Nepal">Nepal</a> and the president of <a href="/wiki/Sri_Lanka" title="Sri Lanka">Sri Lanka</a>). Bangladesh helped found SAARC.</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>The first major intergovernmental organization joined by Bangladesh was the <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_Nations" title="Commonwealth of Nations">Commonwealth of Nations</a> in 1972. The country joined the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a> in 1974, and has been elected twice to the <a href="/wiki/UN_Security_Council" class="mw-redirect" title="UN Security Council">UN Security Council</a>. Ambassador <a href="/wiki/Humayun_Rashid_Choudhury" title="Humayun Rashid Choudhury">Humayun Rashid Choudhury</a> was elected president of the <a href="/wiki/UN_General_Assembly" class="mw-redirect" title="UN General Assembly">UN General Assembly</a> in 1986. Bangladesh relies on <a href="/wiki/Multilateralism" title="Multilateralism">multilateral</a> diplomacy in the <a href="/wiki/World_Trade_Organization" title="World Trade Organization">World Trade Organization</a>. It is a major contributor to <a href="/wiki/UN_peacekeeping" class="mw-redirect" title="UN peacekeeping">UN peacekeeping</a>, providing 113,000 personnel to 54 UN missions in the Middle East, the Balkans, Africa and the Caribbean in 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">[129]</a></sup></p>\n<p>In addition to membership in the Commonwealth and the United Nations, Bangladesh pioneered regional cooperation in <a href="/wiki/South_Asia" title="South Asia">South Asia</a>. Bangladesh is a founding member of the <a href="/wiki/South_Asian_Association_for_Regional_Cooperation" title="South Asian Association for Regional Cooperation">South Asian Association for Regional Cooperation</a> (SAARC), an organization designed to strengthen relations and promote economic and cultural growth among its members. It has hosted several summits, and two Bangladeshi diplomats were the organization\'s secretary-general.</p>\n<p>Bangladesh joined the <a href="/wiki/Organization_of_Islamic_Cooperation" class="mw-redirect" title="Organization of Islamic Cooperation">Organization of Islamic Cooperation</a> (OIC) in 1973. It has hosted the summit of OIC foreign ministers, which addresses issues, conflicts and disputes affecting <a href="/wiki/Muslim_world" title="Muslim world">Muslim-majority countries</a>. Bangladesh is a founding member of the <a href="/wiki/Developing_8_Countries" class="mw-redirect" title="Developing 8 Countries">Developing 8 Countries</a>, a bloc of eight Muslim-majority republics.</p>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Japan" title="Japan">Japan</a> is Bangladesh\'s largest economic-aid provider, and the countries have common political goals.<sup id="cite_ref-books.google.com.bd_130-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-books.google.com.bd-130">[130]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">[131]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a> has longstanding <a href="/wiki/Bangladesh-United_Kingdom_relations" class="mw-redirect" title="Bangladesh-United Kingdom relations">economic, cultural and military links</a> with Bangladesh. The <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a> is a major <a href="/wiki/Bangladesh-United_States_relations" class="mw-redirect" title="Bangladesh-United States relations">economic and security partner</a>, including its largest export market and foreign investor. Seventy-six percent of <a href="/wiki/Bangladeshis" title="Bangladeshis">Bangladeshis</a> viewed the United States favorably in 2014, one of the highest ratings among <a href="/wiki/Asia" title="Asia">Asian</a> countries.<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">[132]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">[133]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a> is Bangladesh\'s largest regional market, conducting <a href="/wiki/Public_diplomacy" title="Public diplomacy">public diplomacy</a> and providing development assistance.</p>\n<p>Relations with other countries are generally positive. Shared democratic values ease relations with Western countries, and similar economic concerns forge ties to other <a href="/wiki/Developing_countries" class="mw-redirect" title="Developing countries">developing countries</a>. Despite poor working conditions and war affecting overseas <a href="/wiki/Bangladeshis_in_the_Middle_East" title="Bangladeshis in the Middle East">Bangladeshi workers</a>, relations with <a href="/wiki/Middle_East" title="Middle East">Middle Eastern</a> countries are friendly and bounded by religion and culture; more than a million Bangladeshis are employed in the region. In 2016, the <a href="/wiki/King_of_Saudi_Arabia" title="King of Saudi Arabia">king of Saudi Arabia</a> called Bangladesh "one of the most important Muslim countries".<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">[134]</a></sup></p>\n<div class="thumb tleft">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Russia-Bangladeshi_talks_Moscow_2013-01-15_03.jpeg" class="image"><img alt="A seated Sheikh Hasina and Vladimir Putin smile at each other across a small table" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/Russia-Bangladeshi_talks_Moscow_2013-01-15_03.jpeg/220px-Russia-Bangladeshi_talks_Moscow_2013-01-15_03.jpeg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/Russia-Bangladeshi_talks_Moscow_2013-01-15_03.jpeg/330px-Russia-Bangladeshi_talks_Moscow_2013-01-15_03.jpeg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/Russia-Bangladeshi_talks_Moscow_2013-01-15_03.jpeg/440px-Russia-Bangladeshi_talks_Moscow_2013-01-15_03.jpeg 2x" data-file-width="650" data-file-height="434" /></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Russia-Bangladeshi_talks_Moscow_2013-01-15_03.jpeg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\n<a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Bangladesh" title="Prime Minister of Bangladesh">Prime Minister of Bangladesh</a> <a href="/wiki/Sheikh_Hasina" title="Sheikh Hasina">Sheikh Hasina</a> and <a href="/wiki/President_of_Russia" title="President of Russia">President of Russia</a> <a href="/wiki/Vladimir_Putin" title="Vladimir Putin">Vladimir Putin</a> in Moscow, 2013</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>Bangladesh\'s most politically-important bilateral relationship is with neighboring <a href="/wiki/India" title="India">India</a>. In 2015, major Indian newspapers called Bangladesh a "trusted friend".<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">[135]</a></sup> Bangladesh and India are South Asia\'s largest trading partners. The countries are forging regional economic and infrastructure projects, such as a regional motor-vehicle agreement in <a href="/wiki/Eastern_South_Asia" title="Eastern South Asia">eastern South Asia</a> and a coastal shipping agreement in the <a href="/wiki/Bay_of_Bengal" title="Bay of Bengal">Bay of Bengal</a>. <a href="/wiki/Bangladesh-India_relations" class="mw-redirect" title="Bangladesh-India relations">Indo-Bangladesh relations</a> have a shared cultural heritage and democratic values and a history of support for <a href="/wiki/Bangladesh_Liberation_War" title="Bangladesh Liberation War">Bangladeshi independence</a>. Despite political goodwill, <a href="/wiki/Deaths_along_the_Bangladesh%E2%80%93India_border" title="Deaths along the Bangladesh\xe2\x80\x93India border">border killings of Bangladeshi civilians</a> and the lack of a comprehensive water-sharing agreement for 54 trans-boundary rivers are major issues. In 2017, India joined Russia and China in refusing to condemn Myanmar\'s atrocities against the <a href="/wiki/Rohingya" class="mw-redirect" title="Rohingya">Rohingya</a>, which contradicted with Bangladesh\'s demand for recognizing Rohingya human rights.<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">[136]</a></sup> However, the Indian air force delivered aid shipments for Rohingya refugees in Bangladesh.<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">[137]</a></sup> The rise of <a href="/wiki/Hindu_extremism" class="mw-redirect" title="Hindu extremism">Hindu extremism</a> and <a href="/wiki/Islamophobia" title="Islamophobia">Islamophobia</a> in India has also affected Bangladesh. The Bangladeshi <a href="/wiki/Beef" title="Beef">beef</a> and <a href="/wiki/Leather" title="Leather">leather</a> industries have seen increased prices due to the Indian <a href="/wiki/Bharatiya_Janata_Party" title="Bharatiya Janata Party">BJP</a> government\'s Hindu nationalist campaign against the export of beef and cattle skin.<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">[138]</a></sup></p>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Bangladesh-China_relations" class="mw-redirect" title="Bangladesh-China relations">Sino-Bangladesh relations</a> date to the 1950s and are relatively warm, despite the Chinese leadership siding with Pakistan during Bangladesh\'s war of independence. China and Bangladesh established bilateral relations in 1976 which have significantly strengthened, and the country is considered a cost-effective source of arms for the Bangladeshi military.<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">[139]</a></sup> Since the 1980s 80 percent of Bangladesh\'s military equipment has been supplied by China (often with generous credit terms), and China is Bangladesh\'s largest trading partner. Both countries are part of the <a href="/wiki/BCIM_Forum" title="BCIM Forum">BCIM Forum</a>.</p>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Secretary_Kerry_Holds_a_One-On-One_Chat_With_Bangladeshi_Foreign_Minister_Mahmoud_Ali_In_Dhaka_(28692597843).jpg" class="image"><img alt="A. H. Mahmud Ali and John Kerry, seated closely together and talking" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Secretary_Kerry_Holds_a_One-On-One_Chat_With_Bangladeshi_Foreign_Minister_Mahmoud_Ali_In_Dhaka_%2828692597843%29.jpg/220px-Secretary_Kerry_Holds_a_One-On-One_Chat_With_Bangladeshi_Foreign_Minister_Mahmoud_Ali_In_Dhaka_%2828692597843%29.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Secretary_Kerry_Holds_a_One-On-One_Chat_With_Bangladeshi_Foreign_Minister_Mahmoud_Ali_In_Dhaka_%2828692597843%29.jpg/330px-Secretary_Kerry_Holds_a_One-On-One_Chat_With_Bangladeshi_Foreign_Minister_Mahmoud_Ali_In_Dhaka_%2828692597843%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Secretary_Kerry_Holds_a_One-On-One_Chat_With_Bangladeshi_Foreign_Minister_Mahmoud_Ali_In_Dhaka_%2828692597843%29.jpg/440px-Secretary_Kerry_Holds_a_One-On-One_Chat_With_Bangladeshi_Foreign_Minister_Mahmoud_Ali_In_Dhaka_%2828692597843%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4180" data-file-height="2787" /></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Secretary_Kerry_Holds_a_One-On-One_Chat_With_Bangladeshi_Foreign_Minister_Mahmoud_Ali_In_Dhaka_(28692597843).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\n<a href="/wiki/US_Secretary_of_State" class="mw-redirect" title="US Secretary of State">US Secretary of State</a> <a href="/wiki/John_Kerry" title="John Kerry">John Kerry</a> and <a href="/wiki/Foreign_Minister_of_Bangladesh" class="mw-redirect" title="Foreign Minister of Bangladesh">Foreign Minister of Bangladesh</a> <a href="/wiki/A._H._Mahmud_Ali" class="mw-redirect" title="A. H. Mahmud Ali">A. H. Mahmud Ali</a> in Dhaka, 2016</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>The neighbouring country of <a href="/wiki/Myanmar" title="Myanmar">Myanmar</a> was one of first countries to recognize Bangladesh.<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">[140]</a></sup> Despite common regional interests, Bangladesh-Myanmar relations have been strained by the <a href="/wiki/Rohingya" class="mw-redirect" title="Rohingya">Rohingya</a> refugee issue and the isolationist policies of the Myanmar military. In 2012, the countries came to terms at the <a href="/wiki/International_Tribunal_for_the_Law_of_the_Sea" title="International Tribunal for the Law of the Sea">International Tribunal for the Law of the Sea</a> over maritime disputes in the Bay of Bengal.<sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">[141]</a></sup> In 2016 and 2017, relations with Myanmar again strained as over 400,000 <a href="/wiki/Rohingya_refugees_in_Bangladesh" title="Rohingya refugees in Bangladesh">Rohingya refugees</a> entered Bangladesh after atrocities. The parliament, government and civil society of Bangladesh have been at the forefront of <a href="/wiki/International_reaction_to_the_2016-17_Rohingya_exodus" class="mw-redirect" title="International reaction to the 2016-17 Rohingya exodus">international criticism</a> against Myanmar for military operations against the Rohingya, which the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a> has described as <a href="/wiki/Ethnic_cleansing" title="Ethnic cleansing">ethnic cleansing</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">[142]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">[143]</a></sup></p>\n<p>Pakistan and Bangladesh have a US$550 million trade relationship,<sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">[144]</a></sup> particularly in Pakistani <a href="/wiki/Cotton" title="Cotton">cotton</a> imports for the Bangladeshi textile industry. Although Bangladeshi and Pakistani businesses have invested in each other, diplomatic relations are strained because of Pakistani denial of the <a href="/wiki/1971_Bangladesh_genocide" title="1971 Bangladesh genocide">1971 Bangladesh genocide</a>.</p>\n<p>Bangladeshi aid agencies work in many developing countries. An example is <a href="/wiki/BRAC_(NGO)" title="BRAC (NGO)">BRAC</a> in <a href="/wiki/Afghanistan" title="Afghanistan">Afghanistan</a>, which benefits 12 million people in that country.<sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">[145]</a></sup> Bangladesh has a record of <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_nonproliferation" class="mw-redirect" title="Nuclear nonproliferation">nuclear nonproliferation</a> as a party to the <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_Nonproliferation_Treaty" class="mw-redirect" title="Nuclear Nonproliferation Treaty">Nuclear Nonproliferation Treaty</a> (NPT) and the <a href="/wiki/Comprehensive_Test_Ban_Treaty" class="mw-redirect" title="Comprehensive Test Ban Treaty">Comprehensive Test Ban Treaty</a> (CTBT).<sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146">[146]</a></sup> It is a state party to the <a href="/wiki/Rome_Statute_of_the_International_Criminal_Court" title="Rome Statute of the International Criminal Court">Rome Statute of the International Criminal Court</a>.</p>\n<p>Bangladeshi foreign policy is influenced by the principle of "friendship to all and malice to none", first articulated by Bengali statesman <a href="/wiki/H._S._Suhrawardy" class="mw-redirect" title="H. S. Suhrawardy">H. S. Suhrawardy</a> in 1957.<sup id="cite_ref-books.google.com.bd_130-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-books.google.com.bd-130">[130]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147">[147]</a></sup> Suhrawardy led East and West Pakistan to join the <a href="/wiki/Southeast_Asia_Treaty_Organization" title="Southeast Asia Treaty Organization">Southeast Asia Treaty Organization</a>, <a href="/wiki/CENTO" class="mw-redirect" title="CENTO">CENTO</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Regional_Cooperation_for_Development" title="Regional Cooperation for Development">Regional Cooperation for Development</a>.</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Human_rights">Human rights</span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Human_rights_in_Bangladesh" title="Human rights in Bangladesh">Human rights in Bangladesh</a></div>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Laws_in_Bangladesh" title="Laws in Bangladesh">Rights in Bangladesh</a> are enshrined in the country\'s constitution. However, government and security forces have flouted constitutional principles and have been accused of <a href="/wiki/Human_rights" title="Human rights">human rights</a> abuses. Bangladesh is ranked "partly free" in <a href="/wiki/Freedom_House" title="Freedom House">Freedom House</a>\'s <i><a href="/wiki/Freedom_in_the_World" title="Freedom in the World">Freedom in the World</a></i> report,<sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148">[148]</a></sup> but its press is ranked "not free".<sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149">[149]</a></sup> According to the British <a href="/wiki/Economist_Intelligence_Unit" title="Economist Intelligence Unit">Economist Intelligence Unit</a>, the country has a <a href="/wiki/Hybrid_regime" class="mw-redirect" title="Hybrid regime">hybrid regime</a>: the third of four rankings in its <a href="/wiki/Democracy_Index" title="Democracy Index">Democracy Index</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150">[150]</a></sup> Bangladesh was the third-most-peaceful South Asian country in the 2015 <a href="/wiki/Global_Peace_Index" title="Global Peace Index">Global Peace Index</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151">[151]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Civil_society" title="Civil society">Civil society</a> and <a href="/wiki/Media_in_Bangladesh" class="mw-redirect" title="Media in Bangladesh">media in Bangladesh</a> have been attacked by the ruling <a href="/wiki/Bangladesh_Awami_League" title="Bangladesh Awami League">Awami League</a> government and <a href="/wiki/Islamic_extremist" class="mw-redirect" title="Islamic extremist">Islamic extremists</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-thedailystar.net_152-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-thedailystar.net-152">[152]</a></sup></p>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Rapid_Action_Battalion_(04).jpg" class="image"><img alt="Armed men in black uniforms on a street" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/Rapid_Action_Battalion_%2804%29.jpg/220px-Rapid_Action_Battalion_%2804%29.jpg" width="220" height="185" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/Rapid_Action_Battalion_%2804%29.jpg/330px-Rapid_Action_Battalion_%2804%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/Rapid_Action_Battalion_%2804%29.jpg/440px-Rapid_Action_Battalion_%2804%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2913" data-file-height="2447" /></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Rapid_Action_Battalion_(04).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nBangladeshi law-enforcement agencies, including the Rapid Action Battalion <i>(pictured)</i>, have been accused of human-rights abuses.</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>According to National Human Rights Commission chairman Mizanur Rahman, 70% of alleged human-rights violations are committed by law-enforcement agencies.<sup id="cite_ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153">[153]</a></sup> Targets have included <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Peace_Prize" title="Nobel Peace Prize">Nobel Peace Prize</a> winner <a href="/wiki/Muhammad_Yunus" title="Muhammad Yunus">Muhammad Yunus</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Grameen_Bank" title="Grameen Bank">Grameen Bank</a>, <a href="/wiki/Attacks_on_secularists_in_Bangladesh" class="mw-redirect" title="Attacks on secularists in Bangladesh">secularist bloggers</a> and independent and pro-opposition newspapers and television networks. The United Nations is concerned about government "measures that restrict freedom of expression and democratic space".<sup id="cite_ref-thedailystar.net_152-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-thedailystar.net-152">[152]</a></sup></p>\n<p>Bangladeshi security forces, particularly the <a href="/wiki/Rapid_Action_Battalion" title="Rapid Action Battalion">Rapid Action Battalion</a> (RAB), have received international condemnation for human-rights abuses (including <a href="/wiki/Enforced_disappearances" class="mw-redirect" title="Enforced disappearances">enforced disappearances</a>, <a href="/wiki/Torture" title="Torture">torture</a> and <a href="/wiki/Extrajudicial_killing" title="Extrajudicial killing">extrajudicial killings</a>). Over 1,000 people have been said to have been victims of extrajudicial killings by RAB since its inception under the last <a href="/wiki/Bangladesh_Nationalist_Party" title="Bangladesh Nationalist Party">Bangladesh Nationalist Party</a> government.<sup id="cite_ref-154" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-154">[154]</a></sup> The RAB has been called a "death squad" by <a href="/wiki/Human_Rights_Watch" title="Human Rights Watch">Human Rights Watch</a> and <a href="/wiki/Amnesty_International" title="Amnesty International">Amnesty International</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-hrw.org_155-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hrw.org-155">[155]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-dw.com_156-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dw.com-156">[156]</a></sup> which have called for the force to be disbanded.<sup id="cite_ref-hrw.org_155-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hrw.org-155">[155]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-dw.com_156-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dw.com-156">[156]</a></sup> The British and American governments have been criticized for funding and engaging the force in counter-terrorism operations.<sup id="cite_ref-157" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-157">[157]</a></sup></p>\n<p>The Bangladeshi government has not fully implemented the <a href="/wiki/Chittagong_Hill_Tracts_Peace_Accord" title="Chittagong Hill Tracts Peace Accord">Chittagong Hill Tracts Peace Accord</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-158" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-158">[158]</a></sup> The Hill Tracts region remains heavily <a href="/wiki/Militarized" class="mw-redirect" title="Militarized">militarized</a>, despite a peace treaty with <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Indigenous people">indigenous people</a> forged by the <a href="/wiki/Parbatya_Chattagram_Jana_Samhati_Samiti" title="Parbatya Chattagram Jana Samhati Samiti">United People\'s Party of the Chittagong Hill Tracts</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-159" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-159">[159]</a></sup></p>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Secularism" title="Secularism">Secularism</a> is protected by the <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Bangladesh" title="Constitution of Bangladesh">constitution of Bangladesh</a>, and religious parties are barred from contesting elections; however, the government is accused of courting religious extremist groups. Islam\'s ambiguous position as the <i>de facto</i> <a href="/wiki/State_religion" title="State religion">state religion</a> has been criticized by the United Nations.<sup id="cite_ref-160" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-160">[160]</a></sup> Despite relative harmony, religious minorities have faced occasional persecution. The Hindu and <a href="/wiki/Buddhist" class="mw-redirect" title="Buddhist">Buddhist</a> communities have experienced <a href="/wiki/Religious_violence" title="Religious violence">religious violence</a> from Islamic groups, notably the <a href="/wiki/Bangladesh_Jamaat-e-Islami" title="Bangladesh Jamaat-e-Islami">Bangladesh Jamaat-e-Islami</a> and its student wing (<a href="/wiki/Bangladesh_Islami_Chhatra_Shibir" title="Bangladesh Islami Chhatra Shibir">Shibir</a>). Islamic far-right candidates peaked at 12 percent of the vote in 2001, falling to four percent in 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-161" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-161">[161]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Homosexuality" title="Homosexuality">Homosexuality</a> is outlawed by section 377 of the criminal code, and is punishable by a maximum of life imprisonment.<sup id="cite_ref-162" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-162">[162]</a></sup></p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Corruption">Corruption</span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Corruption_in_Bangladesh" title="Corruption in Bangladesh">Corruption in Bangladesh</a></div>\n<p>Bangladesh was 14th on <a href="/wiki/Transparency_International" title="Transparency International">Transparency International</a>\'s 2014 <a href="/wiki/Corruption_Perceptions_Index" title="Corruption Perceptions Index">Corruption Perceptions Index</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-163" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-163">[163]</a></sup> In 2015, bribes made up 3.7 percent of the national budget.<sup id="cite_ref-164" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-164">[164]</a></sup> The country\'s <a href="/wiki/Anti-Corruption_Commission_(Bangladesh)" title="Anti-Corruption Commission (Bangladesh)">Anti-Corruption Commission</a> was active during the <a href="/wiki/2006%E2%80%9308_Bangladeshi_political_crisis" title="2006\xe2\x80\x9308 Bangladeshi political crisis">2006\xe2\x80\x9308 Bangladeshi political crisis</a>, indicting many leading politicians, bureaucrats and businessmen for <a href="/wiki/Graft_(politics)" title="Graft (politics)">graft</a>. After it assumed power in 2009, the Awami League government reduced the commission\'s independent power to investigate and prosecute.<sup id="cite_ref-165" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-165">[165]</a></sup> Land administration was the sector with the most bribery in 2015,<sup id="cite_ref-166" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-166">[166]</a></sup> followed by education,<sup id="cite_ref-167" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-167">[167]</a></sup> police<sup id="cite_ref-168" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-168">[168]</a></sup> and water supply.<sup id="cite_ref-169" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-169">[169]</a></sup></p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Bangladesh" title="Economy of Bangladesh">Economy of Bangladesh</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_companies_of_Bangladesh" title="List of companies of Bangladesh">List of companies of Bangladesh</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a href="/wiki/File:GulshanDhaka.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Skyline of Dhaka at twilight" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/GulshanDhaka.jpg/300px-GulshanDhaka.jpg" width="300" height="175" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/GulshanDhaka.jpg/450px-GulshanDhaka.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/GulshanDhaka.jpg/600px-GulshanDhaka.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1800" data-file-height="1047" /></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:GulshanDhaka.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nDhaka, the commercial and financial hub of the country, is the largest economic centre in <a href="/wiki/Eastern_South_Asia" title="Eastern South Asia">eastern South Asia</a>.</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>Bangladesh, a <a href="/wiki/Developing_country" title="Developing country">developing country</a> with a market-based <a href="/wiki/Mixed_economy" title="Mixed economy">mixed economy</a>, is one of the <a href="/wiki/Next_Eleven" title="Next Eleven">Next Eleven</a> <a href="/wiki/Emerging_markets" title="Emerging markets">emerging markets</a>. Its per-capita income was <span style="white-space: nowrap"><a href="/wiki/United_States_dollar" title="United States dollar">US$</a>1,190</span> in 2014, with a <a href="/wiki/Gross_domestic_product" title="Gross domestic product">GDP</a> of $209 billion.<sup id="cite_ref-170" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-170">[170]</a></sup> Bangladesh has the third-largest South Asian economy (after India and Pakistan) and the second-highest <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_foreign_exchange_reserves" class="mw-redirect" title="List of countries by foreign exchange reserves">foreign-exchange reserves</a> (after India). The <a href="/wiki/Bangladeshi_diaspora" title="Bangladeshi diaspora">Bangladeshi diaspora</a> contributed $15.31&#160;billion in <a href="/wiki/Remittance_to_Bangladesh" title="Remittance to Bangladesh">remittances</a> in 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-171" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-171">[171]</a></sup></p>\n<p>During its first five years of independence Bangladesh adopted socialist policies, an Awami League blunder.<sup id="cite_ref-172" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-172">[172]</a></sup> The subsequent military regime and BNP and Jatiya Party governments restored free markets and promoted the country\'s private sector. In 1991, finance minister <a href="/wiki/Saifur_Rahman" title="Saifur Rahman">Saifur Rahman</a> introduced a programme of <a href="/wiki/Economic_liberalization" title="Economic liberalization">economic liberalization</a>. The Bangladeshi private sector has rapidly expanded, with a number of <a href="/wiki/List_of_conglomerates_in_Bangladesh" class="mw-redirect" title="List of conglomerates in Bangladesh">conglomerates</a> driving the economy. Major industries include textiles, <a href="/wiki/Pharmaceuticals" class="mw-redirect" title="Pharmaceuticals">pharmaceuticals</a>, shipbuilding, steel, electronics, energy, construction materials, chemicals, ceramics, food processing and leather goods. <a href="/wiki/Export-oriented_industrialization" title="Export-oriented industrialization">Export-oriented industrialization</a> has increased, with <a href="/wiki/Fiscal_year" title="Fiscal year">fiscal year</a> 2014\xe2\x80\x9315 exports of $30 billion.<sup id="cite_ref-173" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-173">[173]</a></sup> Most export earnings are from the <a href="/wiki/Bangladesh_textile_industry" class="mw-redirect" title="Bangladesh textile industry">garment-manufacturing industry</a>. Bangladesh also has <a href="/wiki/Social_enterprise" title="Social enterprise">social enterprises</a>, including the Nobel Peace Prize-winning <a href="/wiki/Grameen_Bank" title="Grameen Bank">Grameen Bank</a> and <a href="/wiki/BRAC_(NGO)" title="BRAC (NGO)">BRAC</a> (the world\'s largest <a href="/wiki/Non-governmental_organisation" class="mw-redirect" title="Non-governmental organisation">non-governmental organisation</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-174" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-174">[174]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-175" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-175">[175]</a></sup></p>\n<p>However, an insufficient power supply is a significant obstacle to Bangladesh\'s economic development. According to the <a href="/wiki/World_Bank" title="World Bank">World Bank</a>, poor governance, corruption and weak public institutions are also major challenges.<sup id="cite_ref-worldbank-brief_176-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-worldbank-brief-176">[176]</a></sup> In April 2010, <a href="/wiki/Standard_%26_Poor%27s" title="Standard &amp; Poor\'s">Standard &amp; Poor\'s</a> gave Bangladesh a BB- long-term <a href="/wiki/Credit_rating" title="Credit rating">credit rating</a>, below India\'s but above those of Pakistan and Sri Lanka.<sup id="cite_ref-177" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-177">[177]</a></sup></p>\n<p>The country is notable for its <a href="/wiki/Soil_fertility" title="Soil fertility">soil fertility</a> land, including the <a href="/wiki/Ganges_Delta" title="Ganges Delta">Ganges Delta</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sylhet_Division" title="Sylhet Division">Sylhet Division</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Chittagong_Hill_Tracts" title="Chittagong Hill Tracts">Chittagong Hill Tracts</a>. Agriculture is the largest sector of the economy, making up 18.6 percent of Bangladesh\'s GDP in November 2010 and employing about 45 percent of the workforce.<sup id="cite_ref-factbook_178-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-factbook-178">[178]</a></sup> The agricultural sector impacts employment generation, poverty alleviation, <a href="/wiki/Human_resources" title="Human resources">human resources</a> development and <a href="/wiki/Food_security" title="Food security">food security</a>. More Bangladeshis earn their living from agriculture than from any other sector. The country is among the top producers of <a href="/wiki/Rice" title="Rice">rice</a> (fourth), <a href="/wiki/Potatoes" class="mw-redirect" title="Potatoes">potatoes</a> (seventh), <a href="/wiki/Tropical_fruits" class="mw-redirect" title="Tropical fruits">tropical fruits</a> (sixth), jute (second), and farmed fish (fifth).<sup id="cite_ref-FAOSTAT_Production_statistics_2008_179-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FAOSTAT_Production_statistics_2008-179">[179]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-180" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-180">[180]</a></sup></p>\n<p>Bangladesh is the seventh-largest <a href="/wiki/Natural_gas_in_Bangladesh" class="mw-redirect" title="Natural gas in Bangladesh">natural gas producer</a> in Asia, ahead of neighboring Myanmar, and 56 percent of the country\'s electricity is generated by natural gas. Major gas fields are located in the northeastern (particularly Sylhet) and southern (including Barisal and Chittagong) regions. <a href="/wiki/Petrobangla" title="Petrobangla">Petrobangla</a> is the national energy company. The American multinational corporation <a href="/wiki/Chevron_Corporation" title="Chevron Corporation">Chevron</a> produces 50 percent of Bangladesh\'s natural gas.<sup id="cite_ref-181" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-181">[181]</a></sup> According to geologists, the Bay of Bengal contains large, untapped gas reserves in Bangladesh\'s <a href="/wiki/Exclusive_economic_zone" title="Exclusive economic zone">exclusive economic zone</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-182" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-182">[182]</a></sup> Bangladesh has substantial coal reserves, with several coal mines operating in the northwest.</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Dress_Shirt_on_Conveyor_in_a_RMG_factory_of_Bangladesh.JPG" class="image"><img alt="Dress shirts hanging on a production line" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/Dress_Shirt_on_Conveyor_in_a_RMG_factory_of_Bangladesh.JPG/220px-Dress_Shirt_on_Conveyor_in_a_RMG_factory_of_Bangladesh.JPG" width="220" height="214" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/Dress_Shirt_on_Conveyor_in_a_RMG_factory_of_Bangladesh.JPG/330px-Dress_Shirt_on_Conveyor_in_a_RMG_factory_of_Bangladesh.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/1/16/Dress_Shirt_on_Conveyor_in_a_RMG_factory_of_Bangladesh.JPG 2x" data-file-width="346" data-file-height="336" /></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Dress_Shirt_on_Conveyor_in_a_RMG_factory_of_Bangladesh.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nShirt production line in a Bangladeshi factory. Bangladesh is the world\'s second-largest textile exporter, after China.</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>Jute exports remain significant, although the global jute trade has shrunk considerably since its World War II peak. Bangladesh has one of the world\'s oldest tea industries, and is a major exporter of fish and seafood.</p>\n<p>Bangladesh\'s textile and <a href="/wiki/Bangladeshi_RMG_Sector" class="mw-redirect" title="Bangladeshi RMG Sector">ready-made garment</a> industries are the country\'s largest manufacturing sector, with 2014 exports of $25 billion.<sup id="cite_ref-183" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-183">[183]</a></sup> Leather-goods manufacturing, particularly footwear, is the second-largest export sector. The <a href="/wiki/Pharmaceutical_industry_in_Bangladesh" title="Pharmaceutical industry in Bangladesh">pharmaceutical industry</a> meets 97 percent of domestic demand, and exports to many countries.<sup id="cite_ref-184" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-184">[184]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-185" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-185">[185]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Shipbuilding_in_Bangladesh" title="Shipbuilding in Bangladesh">Shipbuilding</a> has grown rapidly, with exports to Europe.<sup id="cite_ref-186" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-186">[186]</a></sup></p>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Steel_industry_in_Bangladesh" title="Steel industry in Bangladesh">Steel</a> is concentrated in the port city of Chittagong, and the <a href="/wiki/Ceramics_industry_in_Bangladesh" title="Ceramics industry in Bangladesh">ceramics industry</a> is prominent in international trade. In 2005 Bangladesh was the world\'s 20th-largest <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_cement_production" title="List of countries by cement production">cement</a> producer, an industry dependent on <a href="/wiki/Limestone" title="Limestone">limestone</a> imports from <a href="/wiki/Northeast_India" class="mw-redirect" title="Northeast India">northeast India</a>. <a href="/wiki/Food_processing" title="Food processing">Food processing</a> is a major sector, with local brands such as <a href="/wiki/PRAN" title="PRAN">PRAN</a> increasing their international market share. The <a href="/wiki/Electronics_industry_in_Bangladesh" title="Electronics industry in Bangladesh">electronics industry</a> is growing rapidly, particularly the <a href="/wiki/Walton_Group" title="Walton Group">Walton Group</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-187" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-187">[187]</a></sup> Bangladesh\'s defense industry includes the <a href="/wiki/Bangladesh_Ordnance_Factories" title="Bangladesh Ordnance Factories">Bangladesh Ordnance Factories</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Khulna_Shipyard" title="Khulna Shipyard">Khulna Shipyard</a>.</p>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Citibank_dhaka.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Modern glass building" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/Citibank_dhaka.jpg/220px-Citibank_dhaka.jpg" width="220" height="267" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/Citibank_dhaka.jpg/330px-Citibank_dhaka.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/Citibank_dhaka.jpg/440px-Citibank_dhaka.jpg 2x" data-file-width="488" data-file-height="592" /></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Citibank_dhaka.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\n<a href="/wiki/Citigroup" title="Citigroup">Citigroup</a>\'s Bangladesh headquarters in Dhaka</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>The service sector accounts for 51 percent of the country\'s GDP. Bangladesh ranks with Pakistan as South Asia\'s second-largest banking sector.<sup id="cite_ref-188" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-188">[188]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Dhaka_Stock_Exchange" title="Dhaka Stock Exchange">Dhaka</a> and <a href="/wiki/Chittagong_Stock_Exchange" title="Chittagong Stock Exchange">Chittagong Stock Exchanges</a> are the country\'s twin financial markets. Bangladesh\'s <a href="/wiki/Telecommunications_in_Bangladesh" title="Telecommunications in Bangladesh">telecommunications industry</a> is one of the world\'s fastest-growing, with 114 million cellphone subscribers in December 2013,<sup id="cite_ref-189" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-189">[189]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Grameenphone" title="Grameenphone">Grameenphone</a>, <a href="/wiki/Banglalink" title="Banglalink">Banglalink</a>, <a href="/wiki/Robi" title="Robi">Robi</a> and <a href="/wiki/BTTB" class="mw-redirect" title="BTTB">BTTB</a> are major companies. <a href="/wiki/Tourism_in_Bangladesh" title="Tourism in Bangladesh">Tourism</a> is developing, with the beach resort of <a href="/wiki/Cox%27s_Bazar" title="Cox\'s Bazar">Cox\'s Bazar</a> the center of the industry. The Sylhet region, home to Bangladesh\'s tea country, also hosts a large number of visitors. The country has <a href="/wiki/List_of_World_Heritage_Sites_in_Bangladesh" title="List of World Heritage Sites in Bangladesh">three UNESCO World Heritage Sites</a> (<a href="/wiki/Historic_Mosque_City_of_Bagerhat" class="mw-redirect" title="Historic Mosque City of Bagerhat">the Mosque City</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ruins_of_the_Buddhist_Vihara_at_Paharpur" class="mw-redirect" title="Ruins of the Buddhist Vihara at Paharpur">the Buddhist Vihara</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Sundarbans" title="Sundarbans">Sundarbans</a>) and five <a href="/wiki/World_Heritage_Site#Nominating_process" title="World Heritage Site">tentative-list</a> sites.<sup id="cite_ref-190" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-190">[190]</a></sup></p>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Microfinance" title="Microfinance">Microfinance</a> was pioneered in Bangladesh by <a href="/wiki/Muhammad_Yunus" title="Muhammad Yunus">Muhammad Yunus</a>. In 2015, the country had over 35&#160;million <a href="/wiki/Microcredit" title="Microcredit">microcredit</a> borrowers.<sup id="cite_ref-191" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-191">[191]</a></sup></p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Transport">Transport</span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Transport_in_Bangladesh" title="Transport in Bangladesh">Transport in Bangladesh</a></div>\n<p>Transport is a major sector of the economy. Aviation has grown rapidly, and includes the <a href="/wiki/Flag_carrier" title="Flag carrier">flag carrier</a> <a href="/wiki/Biman_Bangladesh_Airlines" title="Biman Bangladesh Airlines">Biman Bangladesh Airlines</a> and other <a href="/wiki/List_of_airlines_of_Bangladesh" title="List of airlines of Bangladesh">privately owned airlines</a>. Bangladesh has a <a href="/wiki/List_of_airports_in_Bangladesh" title="List of airports in Bangladesh">number of airports</a>: three international and several domestic and <a href="/wiki/STOL" title="STOL">STOL</a> (short takeoff and landing) airports. The busiest, <a href="/wiki/Shahjalal_International_Airport" title="Shahjalal International Airport">Shahjalal International Airport</a> connects Dhaka with major destinations.</p>\n<p>Bangladesh has a 2,706-kilometre (1,681-mile) rail network operated by state-owned <a href="/wiki/Bangladesh_Railway" title="Bangladesh Railway">Bangladesh Railway</a>. The total length of the country\'s <a href="/wiki/List_of_roads_in_Bangladesh" title="List of roads in Bangladesh">road and highway network</a> is nearly 21,000-kilometre (13,000-mile).</p>\n<p>It has one of the largest inland <a href="/wiki/Waterway" title="Waterway">waterway</a> networks in the world,<sup id="cite_ref-192" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-192">[192]</a></sup> with 8,046 kilometres (5,000 miles) of navigable waters. The southeastern port of Chittagong is its busiest seaport, handling over $60 billion in annual trade (more than 80 percent of the country\'s export-import commerce).<sup id="cite_ref-193" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-193">[193]</a></sup> The second-busiest seaport is <a href="/wiki/Port_of_Mongla" title="Port of Mongla">Mongla</a>. Bangladesh has three <a href="/wiki/Seaport" class="mw-redirect" title="Seaport">seaports</a> and 22 <a href="/wiki/River_port" class="mw-redirect" title="River port">river ports</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-194" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-194">[194]</a></sup></p>\n<table class="infobox" style="text-align:center; width:97%; margin-right:10px; font-size:90%">\n<caption>Top maritime and inland ports</caption>\n<tr>\n<th rowspan="23"><br />\n<p><a href="/wiki/File:Chittagong_Port_Area_12.jpg" class="image" title="Port of Chittagong"><img alt="Port of Chittagong"
