port</td>\n<td></td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="5" style="text-align:center; background:#f5f5f5;"></td>\n</tr>\n</table>\n<div style="clear:both;"></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Energy">Energy</span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Electricity_sector_in_Bangladesh" title="Electricity sector in Bangladesh">Electricity sector in Bangladesh</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_energy_in_Bangladesh" title="Nuclear energy in Bangladesh">Nuclear energy in Bangladesh</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Natural_gas_and_petroleum_in_Bangladesh" title="Natural gas and petroleum in Bangladesh">Natural gas and petroleum in Bangladesh</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a href="/wiki/File:%E0%A6%AC%E0%A6%BE%E0%A6%82%E0%A6%B2%E0%A6%BE%E0%A6%A6%E0%A7%87%E0%A6%B6%E0%A7%87%E0%A6%B0_%E0%A6%95%E0%A6%AF%E0%A6%BC%E0%A6%B2%E0%A6%BE_%E0%A6%93_%E0%A6%97%E0%A7%8D%E0%A6%AF%E0%A6%BE%E0%A6%B8_%E0%A6%AB%E0%A6%BF%E0%A6%B2%E0%A7%8D%E0%A6%A1.png" class="image"><img alt="Map of Bangladesh, illustrating coal and gas deposits" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/%E0%A6%AC%E0%A6%BE%E0%A6%82%E0%A6%B2%E0%A6%BE%E0%A6%A6%E0%A7%87%E0%A6%B6%E0%A7%87%E0%A6%B0_%E0%A6%95%E0%A6%AF%E0%A6%BC%E0%A6%B2%E0%A6%BE_%E0%A6%93_%E0%A6%97%E0%A7%8D%E0%A6%AF%E0%A6%BE%E0%A6%B8_%E0%A6%AB%E0%A6%BF%E0%A6%B2%E0%A7%8D%E0%A6%A1.png/250px-%E0%A6%AC%E0%A6%BE%E0%A6%82%E0%A6%B2%E0%A6%BE%E0%A6%A6%E0%A7%87%E0%A6%B6%E0%A7%87%E0%A6%B0_%E0%A6%95%E0%A6%AF%E0%A6%BC%E0%A6%B2%E0%A6%BE_%E0%A6%93_%E0%A6%97%E0%A7%8D%E0%A6%AF%E0%A6%BE%E0%A6%B8_%E0%A6%AB%E0%A6%BF%E0%A6%B2%E0%A7%8D%E0%A6%A1.png" width="250" height="322" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/%E0%A6%AC%E0%A6%BE%E0%A6%82%E0%A6%B2%E0%A6%BE%E0%A6%A6%E0%A7%87%E0%A6%B6%E0%A7%87%E0%A6%B0_%E0%A6%95%E0%A6%AF%E0%A6%BC%E0%A6%B2%E0%A6%BE_%E0%A6%93_%E0%A6%97%E0%A7%8D%E0%A6%AF%E0%A6%BE%E0%A6%B8_%E0%A6%AB%E0%A6%BF%E0%A6%B2%E0%A7%8D%E0%A6%A1.png/375px-%E0%A6%AC%E0%A6%BE%E0%A6%82%E0%A6%B2%E0%A6%BE%E0%A6%A6%E0%A7%87%E0%A6%B6%E0%A7%87%E0%A6%B0_%E0%A6%95%E0%A6%AF%E0%A6%BC%E0%A6%B2%E0%A6%BE_%E0%A6%93_%E0%A6%97%E0%A7%8D%E0%A6%AF%E0%A6%BE%E0%A6%B8_%E0%A6%AB%E0%A6%BF%E0%A6%B2%E0%A7%8D%E0%A6%A1.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/6/6d/%E0%A6%AC%E0%A6%BE%E0%A6%82%E0%A6%B2%E0%A6%BE%E0%A6%A6%E0%A7%87%E0%A6%B6%E0%A7%87%E0%A6%B0_%E0%A6%95%E0%A6%AF%E0%A6%BC%E0%A6%B2%E0%A6%BE_%E0%A6%93_%E0%A6%97%E0%A7%8D%E0%A6%AF%E0%A6%BE%E0%A6%B8_%E0%A6%AB%E0%A6%BF%E0%A6%B2%E0%A7%8D%E0%A6%A1.png 2x" data-file-width="454" data-file-height="584" /></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:%E0%A6%AC%E0%A6%BE%E0%A6%82%E0%A6%B2%E0%A6%BE%E0%A6%A6%E0%A7%87%E0%A6%B6%E0%A7%87%E0%A6%B0_%E0%A6%95%E0%A6%AF%E0%A6%BC%E0%A6%B2%E0%A6%BE_%E0%A6%93_%E0%A6%97%E0%A7%8D%E0%A6%AF%E0%A6%BE%E0%A6%B8_%E0%A6%AB%E0%A6%BF%E0%A6%B2%E0%A7%8D%E0%A6%A1.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nCoal and natural-gas fields in Bangladesh, 2011</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>Bangladesh had an installed electrical capacity of 10,289 MW in January 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-195" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-195">[195]</a></sup> About 56 percent of the country\'s commercial energy is generated by natural gas, followed by oil, <a href="/wiki/Hydropower" title="Hydropower">hydropower</a> and coal. Bangladesh has planned to import hydropower from <a href="/wiki/Energy_in_Bhutan" title="Energy in Bhutan">Bhutan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Energy_in_Nepal" title="Energy in Nepal">Nepal</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-196" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-196">[196]</a></sup> Nuclear energy is being developed with Russian support in the <a href="/wiki/Ruppur_Nuclear_Power_Plant" class="mw-redirect" title="Ruppur Nuclear Power Plant">Ruppur Nuclear Power Plant</a> project.<sup id="cite_ref-197" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-197">[197]</a></sup> The country ranks fifth worldwide in the number of <a href="/wiki/Renewable_energy" title="Renewable energy">renewable energy</a> <a href="/wiki/Green_job" title="Green job">green jobs</a>, and solar panels are increasingly used to power urban and off-grid rural areas.<sup id="cite_ref-198" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-198">[198]</a></sup></p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Water">Water</span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Water_supply_and_sanitation_in_Bangladesh" title="Water supply and sanitation in Bangladesh">Water supply and sanitation in Bangladesh</a></div>\n<p>An estimated 98 percent of the country\'s population had access to <a href="/wiki/Improved_water_source" title="Improved water source">improved water sources</a> in 2004<sup id="cite_ref-JMP_199-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JMP-199">[199]</a></sup> (a high percentage for a low-income country), achieved largely through the construction of <a href="/wiki/Hand_pump" title="Hand pump">hand pumps</a> with support from external donors. However, in 1993 it was discovered that much of Bangladesh\'s groundwater (the source of drinking water for 97 percent of the rural population and a significant share of the urban population) is naturally contaminated with arsenic.</p>\n<p>Another challenge is low cost recovery due to low tariffs and poor <a href="/wiki/Economic_efficiency" title="Economic efficiency">economic efficiency</a>, especially in urban areas (where water revenue does not cover operating costs). An estimated 56 percent of the population had access to adequate sanitation facilities in 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-200" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-200">[200]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Community-led_total_sanitation" title="Community-led total sanitation">Community-led total sanitation</a>, addressing the problem of <a href="/wiki/Open_defecation" title="Open defecation">open defecation</a> in rural areas, is credited with improving public health since its introduction in 2000.<sup id="cite_ref-201" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-201">[201]</a></sup></p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Science_and_technology">Science and technology</span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Science_and_technology_in_Bangladesh" title="Science and technology in Bangladesh">Science and technology in Bangladesh</a></div>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Information_technology_in_Bangladesh" title="Information technology in Bangladesh">Information technology in Bangladesh</a> and <a href="/wiki/Biotechnology_and_genetic_engineering_in_Bangladesh" title="Biotechnology and genetic engineering in Bangladesh">Biotechnology and genetic engineering in Bangladesh</a></div>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Bangladesh_Council_of_Scientific_and_Industrial_Research" title="Bangladesh Council of Scientific and Industrial Research">Bangladesh Council of Scientific and Industrial Research</a>, founded in 1973, traces its roots to the East Pakistan Regional Laboratories established in Dhaka (1955), <a href="/wiki/Rajshahi" title="Rajshahi">Rajshahi</a> (1965) and Chittagong (1967). Bangladesh\'s <a href="/wiki/Space_agency" class="mw-redirect" title="Space agency">space agency</a>, <a href="/wiki/SPARRSO" class="mw-redirect" title="SPARRSO">SPARRSO</a>, was founded in 1983 with assistance from the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-202" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-202">[202]</a></sup> Bangladesh plans to launch the <a href="/wiki/Bangabandhu-1" title="Bangabandhu-1">Bangabandhu-1</a> communications satellite in 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-203" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-203">[203]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Bangladesh_Atomic_Energy_Commission" title="Bangladesh Atomic Energy Commission">Bangladesh Atomic Energy Commission</a> operates a <a href="/wiki/TRIGA" title="TRIGA">TRIGA</a> research reactor at its atomic-energy facility in <a href="/wiki/Savar" class="mw-redirect" title="Savar">Savar</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-204" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-204">[204]</a></sup> In 2015, Bangladesh was ranked the 26th global IT outsourcing destination.<sup id="cite_ref-205" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-205">[205]</a></sup></p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_Bangladesh" title="Demographics of Bangladesh">Demographics of Bangladesh</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bengalis" title="Bengalis">Bengalis</a></div>\n<table class="toccolours" style="width:15em;border-spacing: 0;float:right;clear:right;margin:0 0 1em 1em;">\n<tr>\n<th class="navbox-title" colspan="3" style="padding:0.25em;font-size:110%">Population (millions)</th>\n</tr>\n<tr style="font-size:95%">\n<th style="border-bottom:1px solid black;padding:1px;width:3em">Year</th>\n<th style="border-bottom:1px solid black;padding:1px 2px;text-align:right"><abbr title="Population">Pop.</abbr></th>\n<th style="border-bottom:1px solid black;padding:1px;text-align:right"><abbr title="Per annum growth rate">\xc2\xb1% p.a.</abbr></th>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th style="text-align:center;padding:1px">1971</th>\n<td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">67.8</td>\n<td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">\xe2\x80\x94&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th style="text-align:center;padding:1px">1980</th>\n<td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">80.6</td>\n<td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">+1.94%</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th style="text-align:center;padding:1px">1990</th>\n<td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">105.3</td>\n<td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">+2.71%</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th style="text-align:center;padding:1px">2000</th>\n<td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">129.6</td>\n<td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">+2.10%</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th style="text-align:center;padding:1px;border-bottom:1px solid #bbbbbb">2010</th>\n<td style="text-align:right;padding:1px;border-bottom:1px solid #bbbbbb">148.7</td>\n<td style="text-align:right;padding:1px;border-bottom:1px solid #bbbbbb">+1.38%</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th style="text-align:center;padding:1px">2012</th>\n<td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">161.1</td>\n<td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">+4.09%</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="3" style="border-top:1px solid black;font-size:85%;text-align:left">Source: OECD/World Bank<sup id="cite_ref-IEApop2011_206-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IEApop2011-206">[206]</a></sup></td>\n</tr>\n</table>\n<p>Estimates of the Bangladeshi population vary, but 2016 UN data suggests 163 million.<sup id="cite_ref-UN_WPP_5-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UN_WPP-5">[5]</a></sup> The 2011 census estimated 142.3 million,<sup id="cite_ref-207" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-207">[207]</a></sup> much less than 2007\xe2\x80\x932010 estimates of Bangladesh\'s population (150\xe2\x80\x93 170&#160;million). Bangladesh is the world\'s <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_population" class="mw-redirect" title="List of countries by population">eighth-most-populous</a> nation. In 1951, its population was 44 million.<sup id="cite_ref-208" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-208">[208]</a></sup> Bangladesh is the most densely-populated large country in the world, ranking 11th in population density when small countries and city-states are included.<sup id="cite_ref-209" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-209">[209]</a></sup></p>\n<p>The country\'s population-growth rate was among the highest in the world in the 1960s and 1970s, when its population grew from 65 to 110&#160;million. With the promotion of <a href="/wiki/Birth_control" title="Birth control">birth control</a> in the 1980s, Bangladesh\'s growth rate began to slow. Its <a href="/wiki/Total_fertility_rate" title="Total fertility rate">total fertility rate</a> is now 2.55, lower than India\'s (2.58) and Pakistan\'s (3.07). The population is relatively young, with 34 percent aged 15 or younger and five percent 65 or older. Life expectancy at birth was estimated at 70 years in 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_94-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA-94">[94]</a></sup> Despite the rapid economic growth, 43% of the country still lives below the <a href="/wiki/International_poverty_line" class="mw-redirect" title="International poverty line">international poverty line</a> on less than $1.25 per day.<sup id="cite_ref-210" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-210">[210]</a></sup></p>\n<div class="thumb tleft">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Los_microcr%C3%A9ditos_son_de_vital_importancia.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Four smiling people" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Los_microcr%C3%A9ditos_son_de_vital_importancia.jpg/220px-Los_microcr%C3%A9ditos_son_de_vital_importancia.jpg" width="220" height="152" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Los_microcr%C3%A9ditos_son_de_vital_importancia.jpg/330px-Los_microcr%C3%A9ditos_son_de_vital_importancia.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Los_microcr%C3%A9ditos_son_de_vital_importancia.jpg/440px-Los_microcr%C3%A9ditos_son_de_vital_importancia.jpg 2x" data-file-width="960" data-file-height="662" /></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Los_microcr%C3%A9ditos_son_de_vital_importancia.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nBangladeshi <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Peace_Prize" title="Nobel Peace Prize">Nobel Peace Prize</a> laureate <a href="/wiki/Muhammad_Yunus" title="Muhammad Yunus">Muhammad Yunus</a> with the former presidents of <a href="/wiki/Peru" title="Peru">Peru</a></div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Bengali_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Bengali people">Bengalis</a> are 98 percent of the population.<sup id="cite_ref-bn_211-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bn-211">[211]</a></sup> Of Bengalis, <a href="/wiki/Bengali_Muslims" title="Bengali Muslims">Muslims</a> are the majority, followed by <a href="/wiki/Bengali_Hindus" title="Bengali Hindus">Hindus</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bengali_Christians" title="Bengali Christians">Christians</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bengali_Buddhists" title="Bengali Buddhists">Buddhists</a>.</p>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Adivasi" title="Adivasi">Adivasi</a> population includes the <a href="/wiki/Chakma_people" title="Chakma people">Chakma</a>, <a href="/wiki/Marma_people" title="Marma people">Marma</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tanchangya_people" title="Tanchangya people">Tanchangya</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tripuri_people" title="Tripuri people">Tripuri</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kuki_people" title="Kuki people">Kuki</a>, Khiang, Khumi, <a href="/wiki/Murang_people" title="Murang people">Murang</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mru" class="mw-redirect" title="Mru">Mru</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chak_people" title="Chak people">Chak</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lushei" class="mw-redirect" title="Lushei">Lushei</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bawm" class="mw-redirect" title="Bawm">Bawm</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bisnupriya_Manipuri_Society" class="mw-redirect" title="Bisnupriya Manipuri Society">Bishnupriya Manipuri</a>, <a href="/wiki/Khasi_people" title="Khasi people">Khasi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Synteng" class="mw-redirect" title="Synteng">Jaintia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Garo_people" title="Garo people">Garo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Santal" class="mw-redirect" title="Santal">Santal</a>, <a href="/wiki/Munda_people" title="Munda people">Munda</a> and <a href="/wiki/Oraon" class="mw-redirect" title="Oraon">Oraon</a> tribes. The Chittagong Hill Tracts region experienced unrest and an <a href="/wiki/Chittagong_Hill_Tracts_conflict" title="Chittagong Hill Tracts conflict">insurgency</a> from 1975 to 1997 in an autonomy movement by its indigenous people. Although a peace accord was signed in 1997, the region remains militarized.<sup id="cite_ref-rashiduzzaman_212-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rashiduzzaman-212">[212]</a></sup></p>\n<p>Bangladesh is home to a significant <a href="/wiki/Ismaili" class="mw-redirect" title="Ismaili">Ismaili</a> community.<sup id="cite_ref-213" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-213">[213]</a></sup> It hosts many <a href="/wiki/Urdu" title="Urdu">Urdu</a>-speaking immigrants, who migrated there after the partition of India. <a href="/wiki/Stranded_Pakistanis" class="mw-redirect" title="Stranded Pakistanis">Stranded Pakistanis</a> were given citizenship by the Supreme Court in 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-214" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-214">[214]</a></sup></p>\n<p>An estimated over 670,000 <a href="/wiki/Rohingya" class="mw-redirect" title="Rohingya">Rohingya</a> refugees from <a href="/wiki/Myanmar" title="Myanmar">Myanmar</a> live in <a href="/wiki/Refugee_camp" title="Refugee camp">refugee camps</a> in <a href="/wiki/Cox%27s_Bazar_District" title="Cox\'s Bazar District">Cox\'s Bazar District</a> in the southeast.<sup id="cite_ref-215" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-215">[215]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-216" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-216">[216]</a></sup> The region has received influxes of Rohingya refugees during Burmese military crackdowns in 1978, 1991, 2012 and 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-217" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-217">[217]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-218" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-218">[218]</a></sup></p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Urban_centres">Urban centres</span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote Bangladesh</a></div>\n<table class="navbox">\n<tr>\n<th colspan="10" class="navbox-title">\n<div style="float:right; width:6em; height:2.6em">&#160;</div>\n<div class="plainlinks hlist navbar mini" style="text-align: center"><a href="/wiki/File:Gollamari_Sritisoudho.jpg" class="image" title="Khulna"><img alt="Khulna" href="/wiki/Narsingdi_Sadar_Upazila" title="Narsingdi Sadar Upazila">Narsingdi</a></td>\n<td style="text-align:left;"><a href="/wiki/Dhaka_Division" title="Dhaka Division">Dhaka</a></td>\n<td style="text-align:right;">185,128</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td style="text-align:center;background:#f0f0f0;">10</td>\n<td style="text-align:left;"><a href="/wiki/Barisal" title="Barisal">Barisal</a></td>\n<td style="text-align:left;"><a href="/wiki/Barisal_Division" title="Barisal Division">Barisal</a></td>\n<td style="text-align:right;">339,308</td>\n<td style="text-align:center;background:#f0f0f0;">20</td>\n<td style="text-align:left;"><a href="/wiki/Nawabganj_(town)" title="Nawabganj (town)">Nawabganj</a></td>\n<td style="text-align:left;"><a href="/wiki/Rajshahi_Division" title="Rajshahi Division">Rajshahi</a></td>\n<td style="text-align:right;">180,731</td>\n</tr>\n</table>\n<p>Dhaka is Bangladesh\'s capital and largest city. Cities with a <a href="/wiki/City_corporation" class="mw-redirect" title="City corporation">corporation</a> and mayoral elections include Dhaka South, Dhaka North, Chittagong, <a href="/wiki/Khulna" title="Khulna">Khulna</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sylhet" title="Sylhet">Sylhet</a>, Rajshahi, <a href="/wiki/Barisal" title="Barisal">Barisal</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rangpur,_Bangladesh" class="mw-redirect" title="Rangpur, Bangladesh">Rangpur</a>, <a href="/wiki/Comilla" title="Comilla">Comilla</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gazipur,_Dhaka_Division" class="mw-redirect" title="Gazipur, Dhaka Division">Gazipur</a>. Other major cities elect a chairperson; they include Mymensingh, <a href="/wiki/Gopalganj,_Bangladesh" class="mw-redirect" title="Gopalganj, Bangladesh">Gopalganj</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jessore" class="mw-redirect" title="Jessore">Jessore</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bogra" title="Bogra">Bogra</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dinajpur_Sadar" class="mw-redirect" title="Dinajpur Sadar">Dinajpur</a>, <a href="/wiki/Saidpur,_Rangpur_Division" class="mw-redirect" title="Saidpur, Rangpur Division">Saidpur</a>, <a href="/wiki/Narayanganj" title="Narayanganj">Narayanganj</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rangamati" title="Rangamati">Rangamati</a>. Mayors and chairs are elected for five-year terms.</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Languages">Languages</span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_Bangladesh" title="Languages of Bangladesh">Languages of Bangladesh</a></div>\n<p>More than 98 percent of Bangladeshi Bengalis speak Bangla as their native language.<sup id="cite_ref-222" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-222">[222]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-constitution-I-5_223-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-constitution-I-5-223">[223]</a></sup> Regional languages or <a href="/wiki/Bengali_dialects" title="Bengali dialects">dialects</a> are also spoken, which include <a href="/wiki/Chittagonian_language" title="Chittagonian language">Chittagonian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sylheti" class="mw-redirect" title="Sylheti">Sylheti</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rangpuri_language" title="Rangpuri language">Rangpuri</a>. <a href="/wiki/Pakistani_Biharis" class="mw-redirect" title="Pakistani Biharis">Pakistani Biharis</a>, stranded since 1971 and living in Bangladeshi camps, speak <a href="/wiki/Urdu" title="Urdu">Urdu</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-224" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-224">[224]</a></sup> Rohingya refugees from Myanmar, living in Bangladeshi camps since 1978, speak <a href="/wiki/Rohingya_language" title="Rohingya language">Rohingya</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-225" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-225">[225]</a></sup> Several <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_Bangladesh" title="Languages of Bangladesh">indigenous minority languages</a> are also spoken.</p>\n<p>Bangla is the official language,<sup id="cite_ref-3._The_state_language_226-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3._The_state_language-226">[226]</a></sup> but English is sometimes used secondarily for official purposes (especially in the legal system). Although laws were historically written in English, they were not translated into Bangla until 1987. Bangladesh\'s constitution and laws now exist in English and Bangla.<sup id="cite_ref-227" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-227">[227]</a></sup> English is used as a second language by the middle and upper classes, and is widely used in higher education.<sup id="cite_ref-Hasan_228-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hasan-228">[228]</a></sup></p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Religion_in_Bangladesh" title="Religion in Bangladesh">Religion in Bangladesh</a></div>\n<div class="barbox tleft" style="overflow-x: auto;">\n<div style="border:1px solid silver; font-size:88%; padding:0.4em; width:250px; background: white;">\n<table style="border-collapse:collapse; width:100%;">\n<tr style="background:#ddd">\n<th colspan="5">Religions in Bangladesh<sup id="cite_ref-.E0.A6.AC.E0.A6.BE.E0.A6.82.E0.A6.B2.E0.A6.BE.E0.A6.A6.E0.A7.87.E0.A6.B6.E0.A6.95.E0.A7.87_.E0.A6.9C.E0.A6.BE.E0.A6.A8.E0.A7.81.E0.A6.A8_3-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-.E0.A6.AC.E0.A6.BE.E0.A6.82.E0.A6.B2.E0.A6.BE.E0.A6.A6.E0.A7.87.E0.A6.B6.E0.A6.95.E0.A7.87_.E0.A6.9C.E0.A6.BE.E0.A6.A8.E0.A7.81.E0.A6.A8-3">[3]</a></sup></th>\n</tr>\n<tr style="font-size:88%; height:4px;">\n<td style="padding:0 4px;">Religion</td>\n<td style="padding:0 4px; text-align:right;"></td>\n<td style="width:100px;"></td>\n<td style="padding:0 4px; width:1em; text-align:right;">Percent</td>\n<td style="padding:0 4px; text-align:right;"></td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; min-width: 8em;"><a href="/wiki/Islam_in_Bangladesh" title="Islam in Bangladesh">Muslim</a></td>\n<td style="width: 100px; border-left: solid 1px silver; border-right: solid 1px silver;">\n<div style="background:MediumSeaGreen; width:86.6%; overflow: hidden;">&#160;\xe2\x80\x89</div>\n</td>\n<td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; text-align: right;">86.6%</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; min-width: 8em;"><a href="/wiki/Hinduism_in_Bangladesh" title="Hinduism in Bangladesh">Hindu</a></td>\n<td style="width: 100px; border-left: solid 1px silver; border-right: solid 1px silver;">\n<div style="background:DarkOrange; width:12.1%; overflow: hidden;">&#160;\xe2\x80\x89</div>\n</td>\n<td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; text-align: right;">12.1%</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; min-width: 8em;"><a href="/wiki/Buddhism_in_Bangladesh" title="Buddhism in Bangladesh">Buddhist</a></td>\n<td style="width: 100px; border-left: solid 1px silver; border-right: solid 1px silver;">\n<div style="background:Gold; width:0.6%; overflow: hidden;">&#160;\xe2\x80\x89</div>\n</td>\n<td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; text-align: right;">0.6%</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; min-width: 8em;"><a href="/wiki/Christianity_in_Bangladesh" title="Christianity in Bangladesh">Christian</a></td>\n<td style="width: 100px; border-left: solid 1px silver; border-right: solid 1px silver;">\n<div style="background:blue; width:0.4%; overflow: hidden;">&#160;\xe2\x80\x89</div>\n</td>\n<td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; text-align: right;">0.4%</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; min-width: 8em;">Others</td>\n<td style="width: 100px; border-left: solid 1px silver; border-right: solid 1px silver;">\n<div style="background:red; width:0.3%; overflow: hidden;">&#160;\xe2\x80\x89</div>\n</td>\n<td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; text-align: right;">0.3%</td>\n</tr>\n</table>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Islam_in_Bangladesh" title="Islam in Bangladesh">Islam</a> is Bangladesh\'s largest religion, followed by 86.6 percent of the population. The country is home to most <a href="/wiki/Bengali_Muslims" title="Bengali Muslims">Bengali Muslims</a>, the second-largest ethnic group in the Muslim world. Most Bangladeshi Muslims are <a href="/wiki/Sunni" class="mw-redirect" title="Sunni">Sunni</a>, followed by <a href="/wiki/Shia" class="mw-redirect" title="Shia">Shia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ahmadiya" class="mw-redirect" title="Ahmadiya">Ahmadiya</a>. About four percent are <a href="/wiki/Non-denominational_Muslims" class="mw-redirect" title="Non-denominational Muslims">non-denominational Muslims</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-229" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-229">[229]</a></sup> Bangladesh has the fourth-largest Muslim population in the world, and is the third-largest Muslim-majority country (after Indonesia and Pakistan).<sup id="cite_ref-230" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-230">[230]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Sufism" title="Sufism">Sufism</a> has a lengthy heritage in the region.<sup id="cite_ref-231" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-231">[231]</a></sup> The largest gathering of Muslims in Bangladesh is the <a href="/wiki/Bishwa_Ijtema" title="Bishwa Ijtema">Bishwa Ijtema</a>, held annually by the <a href="/wiki/Tablighi_Jamaat" title="Tablighi Jamaat">Tablighi Jamaat</a>. The Ijtema is the second-largest Muslim congregation in the world, after the <a href="/wiki/Hajj" title="Hajj">Hajj</a>.</p>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Chawkbazar_Shahi_Mosque_3_by_Ragib_Hasan.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Old mosque with flags" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/Chawkbazar_Shahi_Mosque_3_by_Ragib_Hasan.jpg/220px-Chawkbazar_Shahi_Mosque_3_by_Ragib_Hasan.jpg" width="220" height="293" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/Chawkbazar_Shahi_Mosque_3_by_Ragib_Hasan.jpg/330px-Chawkbazar_Shahi_Mosque_3_by_Ragib_Hasan.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/Chawkbazar_Shahi_Mosque_3_by_Ragib_Hasan.jpg/440px-Chawkbazar_Shahi_Mosque_3_by_Ragib_Hasan.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="1600" /></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Chawkbazar_Shahi_Mosque_3_by_Ragib_Hasan.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nChawkbazar Shahi Mosque, founded in Dhaksa in 1676</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Hinduism_in_Bangladesh" title="Hinduism in Bangladesh">Hinduism</a> is followed by 12.1 percent of the population; most are <a href="/wiki/Bengali_Hindu" class="mw-redirect" title="Bengali Hindu">Bengali Hindus</a>, and some are <a href="/wiki/Ethnic_groups_in_Bangladesh" class="mw-redirect" title="Ethnic groups in Bangladesh">ethnic people</a>. Bangladeshi Hindus are the country\'s second-largest religious group and the third-largest Hindu community in the world, after those in India and Nepal. Hindus in Bangladesh are fairly evenly distributed, with concentrations in <a href="/wiki/Gopalganj_District,_Bangladesh" title="Gopalganj District, Bangladesh">Gopalganj</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dinajpur_District_(Bangladesh)" class="mw-redirect" title="Dinajpur District (Bangladesh)">Dinajpur</a>, Sylhet, <a href="/wiki/Sunamganj" class="mw-redirect" title="Sunamganj">Sunamganj</a>, Mymensingh, Khulna, Jessore, Chittagong and parts of the Chittagong Hill Tracts. Despite their dwindling numbers, Hindus are the second-largest religious community (after the Muslims) in Dhaka.</p>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Buddhism_in_Bangladesh" title="Buddhism in Bangladesh">Buddhism</a> is the third-largest religion, at 0.6 percent. Bangladeshi Buddhists are concentrated among ethnic groups in the Chittagong Hill Tracts (particularly the Chakma, Marma and Tanchangya peoples), and coastal Chittagong is home to a large number of <a href="/wiki/Bengali_Buddhist" class="mw-redirect" title="Bengali Buddhist">Bengali Buddhists</a>. Christianity is the fourth-largest religion, at 0.4 percent.<sup id="cite_ref-232" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-232">[232]</a></sup> The remaining 0.3 percent of the population observe folk religions and animism.</p>\n<p>The Constitution of Bangladesh declares Islam the state religion, but bans religion-based politics. It proclaims equal recognition of Hindus, Buddhists, Christians and people of all faiths.<sup id="cite_ref-233" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-233">[233]</a></sup> In 1972, Bangladesh was South Asia\'s first constitutionally-secular country.<sup id="cite_ref-234" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-234">[234]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/U._S._State_Department" class="mw-redirect" title="U. S. State Department">U. S. State Department</a> describes Bangladesh as a <a href="/wiki/Secular" class="mw-redirect" title="Secular">secular</a>, pluralistic <a href="/wiki/Democracy" title="Democracy">democracy</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-235" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-235">[235]</a></sup></p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Education_in_Bangladesh" title="Education in Bangladesh">Education in Bangladesh</a></div>\n<p>Bangladesh has a low <a href="/wiki/Literacy_rate" class="mw-redirect" title="Literacy rate">literacy rate</a>, which was estimated at 66.5 percent for males and 63.1 percent for females in 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_94-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA-94">[94]</a></sup> The country\'s educational system is three-tiered and heavily subsidized, with the government operating many schools at the primary, secondary and higher-secondary levels and subsidizing many private schools. In the tertiary-education sector, the Bangladeshi government funds over 15 state universities through the <a href="/wiki/University_Grants_Commission_of_Bangladesh" class="mw-redirect" title="University Grants Commission of Bangladesh">University Grants Commission</a>.</p>\n<p>The education system is divided into five levels: primary (first to fifth grade), junior secondary (sixth to eighth grade), secondary (ninth and tenth grade), higher secondary (11th and 12th grade) and tertiary.<sup id="cite_ref-CompEd_236-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CompEd-236">[236]</a></sup> Five years of secondary education end with a <a href="/wiki/Secondary_School_Certificate" title="Secondary School Certificate">Secondary School Certificate</a> (SSC) examination; since 2009, the Primary Education Closing (PEC) examination has also been given. Students who pass the PEC examination proceed to four years of secondary or matriculation training, culminating in the SSC examination.<sup id="cite_ref-CompEd_236-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CompEd-236">[236]</a></sup></p>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Students_of_Bangladesh_Bank_Colony_High_School_performed_in_Rajat_Jayanti_(01).jpg" class="image"><img alt="Secondary-school students onstage" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Students_of_Bangladesh_Bank_Colony_High_School_performed_in_Rajat_Jayanti_%2801%29.jpg/220px-Students_of_Bangladesh_Bank_Colony_High_School_performed_in_Rajat_Jayanti_%2801%29.jpg" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Students_of_Bangladesh_Bank_Colony_High_School_performed_in_Rajat_Jayanti_%2801%29.jpg/330px-Students_of_Bangladesh_Bank_Colony_High_School_performed_in_Rajat_Jayanti_%2801%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Students_of_Bangladesh_Bank_Colony_High_School_performed_in_Rajat_Jayanti_%2801%29.jpg/440px-Students_of_Bangladesh_Bank_Colony_High_School_performed_in_Rajat_Jayanti_%2801%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4600" data-file-height="3059" /></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Students_of_Bangladesh_Bank_Colony_High_School_performed_in_Rajat_Jayanti_(01).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nBangladeshi schoolchildren performing onstage</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>Students who pass the PEC examination proceed to three years of junior-secondary education, culminating in the <a href="/wiki/Junior_School_Certificate" title="Junior School Certificate">Junior School Certificate</a> (JSC) examination. Students who pass this examination proceed to two years of secondary education, culminating in the SSC examination. Students who pass this examination proceed to two years of higher-secondary education, culminating in the <a href="/wiki/Higher_Secondary_School_Certificate" title="Higher Secondary School Certificate">Higher Secondary School Certificate</a> (HSC) examination.<sup id="cite_ref-CompEd_236-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CompEd-236">[236]</a></sup></p>\n<p>Education is primarily in Bengali, but English is commonly taught and used. Many Muslim families send their children to part-time courses or full-time religious education in Bengali and <a href="/wiki/Arabic_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Arabic language">Arabic</a> in madrasas.<sup id="cite_ref-CompEd_236-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CompEd-236">[236]</a></sup></p>\n<p>Bangladesh conforms with the <a href="/wiki/Education_For_All" title="Education For All">Education For All</a> (EFA) objectives, the <a href="/wiki/Millennium_Development_Goals" title="Millennium Development Goals">Millennium Development Goals</a> (MDG) and international declarations. Article 17 of the <a href="/wiki/Bangladesh_Constitution" class="mw-redirect" title="Bangladesh Constitution">Bangladesh Constitution</a> provides that all children between the ages of six and ten years receive a basic education free of charge.</p>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Universities_in_Bangladesh" title="Universities in Bangladesh">Universities in Bangladesh</a> are of three general types: public (government-owned and -subsidized), private (privately owned universities) and international (operated and funded by international organizations). Bangladesh has 34 public, 64 private and two international <a href="/wiki/List_of_universities_in_Bangladesh" title="List of universities in Bangladesh">universities</a>; <a href="/wiki/Bangladesh_National_University" class="mw-redirect" title="Bangladesh National University">Bangladesh National University</a> has the largest enrollment, and the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Dhaka" title="University of Dhaka">University of Dhaka</a> (established in 1921) is the oldest. <a href="/wiki/Islamic_University_of_Technology" title="Islamic University of Technology">Islamic University of Technology</a>, commonly known as IUT, is a subsidiary of the Organisation of the Islamic Cooperation (OIC, representing 57 countries in Asia, Africa, Europe and South America). <a href="/wiki/Asian_University_for_Women" title="Asian University for Women">Asian University for Women</a> in Chittagong is the preeminent South Asian liberal-arts university for women, representing 14 Asian countries; its faculty hails from notable academic institutions in North America, Europe, Asia, Australia and the Middle East.<sup id="cite_ref-237" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-237">[237]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/BUET" class="mw-redirect" title="BUET">BUET</a>, <a href="/wiki/CUET" class="mw-redirect" title="CUET">CUET</a>, <a href="/wiki/KUET" class="mw-redirect" title="KUET">KUET</a> and <a href="/wiki/RUET" class="mw-redirect" title="RUET">RUET</a> are Bangladesh\'s four public engineering universities. <a href="/wiki/BUTex" class="mw-redirect" title="BUTex">BUTex</a> and <a href="/wiki/DUET" class="mw-redirect" title="DUET">DUET</a> are two specialized engineering universities; BUTex specializes in textile engineering, and DUET offers higher education to diploma engineers. The <a href="/wiki/National_Institute_of_Textile_Engineering_and_Research" title="National Institute of Textile Engineering and Research">NITER</a> is a specialized public-private partnership institute which provides higher education in <a href="/wiki/Textile_engineering" class="mw-redirect" title="Textile engineering">textile engineering</a>. Science and technology universities include <a href="/wiki/SUST" class="mw-redirect" title="SUST">SUST</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pabna_University_of_Science_%26_Technology" title="Pabna University of Science &amp; Technology">PUST</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jessore_University_of_Science_%26_Technology" title="Jessore University of Science &amp; Technology">JUST</a> and <a href="/w/index.php?title=Noakhali_University_of_Science_%26_Technology&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Noakhali University of Science &amp; Technology (page does not exist)">NSTU</a>. Bangladeshi universities are accredited by and affiliated with the <a href="/wiki/University_Grants_Commission_(Bangladesh)" title="University Grants Commission (Bangladesh)">University Grants Commission</a> (UGC), created by Presidential Order 10 in 1973.<sup id="cite_ref-238" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-238">[238]</a></sup></p>\n<p>Medical education is provided by 29 government and private <a href="/wiki/List_of_medical_colleges_in_Bangladesh" title="List of medical colleges in Bangladesh">medical colleges</a>. All medical colleges are affiliated with the <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Health_and_Family_Welfare_(Bangladesh)" title="Ministry of Health and Family Welfare (Bangladesh)">Ministry of Health and Family Welfare</a>.</p>\n<p>Bangladesh\'s 2015 literacy rate rose to 71 percent due to education modernization and improved funding, with 16,087 schools and 2,363 colleges receiving Monthly Pay Order (MPO) facilities. According to education minister <a href="/wiki/Nurul_Islam_Nahid" title="Nurul Islam Nahid">Nurul Islam Nahid</a>, 27,558 madrasas and technical and vocational institutions were enlisted for the facility. 6,036 educational institutions were outside MPO coverage, and the government enlisted 1,624 private schools for MPO in 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-239" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-239">[239]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-240" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-240">[240]</a></sup></p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Health">Health</span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Health_in_Bangladesh" title="Health in Bangladesh">Health in Bangladesh</a></div>\n<p>Health and education levels remain relatively low, although they have improved as poverty levels have decreased. In rural areas, village doctors with little or no formal training constitute 62 percent of healthcare providers practising "modern medicine"; formally-trained providers make up four percent of the total health workforce. A Future Health Systems survey indicated significant deficiencies in the treatment practices of village doctors, with widespread harmful and inappropriate drug prescribing.<sup id="cite_ref-FHS_Research_Brief_2_241-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FHS_Research_Brief_2-241">[241]</a></sup> Receiving health care from informal providers is encouraged.<sup id="cite_ref-242" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-242">[242]</a></sup></p>\n<p>A 2007 study of 1,000 households in rural Bangladesh found that direct payments to formal and informal healthcare providers and indirect costs (loss of earnings because of illness) associated with illness were deterrents to accessing healthcare from qualified providers.<sup id="cite_ref-FHS_Research_Brief_2_241-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FHS_Research_Brief_2-241">[241]</a></sup> A community survey of 6,183 individuals in rural Bangladesh found a gender difference in treatment-seeking behaviour, with women less likely to seek treatment than to men.<sup id="cite_ref-243" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-243">[243]</a></sup> The use of skilled birth attendant (SBA) services, however, rose from 2005 to 2007 among women from all socioeconomic <a href="/wiki/Quantile" title="Quantile">quintiles</a> except the highest.<sup id="cite_ref-244" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-244">[244]</a></sup> A health watch, a pilot community-empowerment tool, was successfully developed and implemented in south-eastern Bangladesh to improve the uptake and monitoring of public-health services.<sup id="cite_ref-245" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-245">[245]</a></sup></p>\n<p>Bangladesh\'s poor health conditions are attributed to the lack of healthcare provision by the government. According to a 2010 World Bank report, 2009 healthcare spending was 3.35 percent of the country\'s GDP.<sup id="cite_ref-apps.who.int_246-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-apps.who.int-246">[246]</a></sup> The number of hospital beds is 3 per 10,000 population.<sup id="cite_ref-247" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-247">[247]</a></sup> Government spending on healthcare that year was 7.9 percent of the total budget; out-of-pocket expenditures totaled 96.5 percent.<sup id="cite_ref-apps.who.int_246-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-apps.who.int-246">[246]</a></sup></p>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Malnutrition" title="Malnutrition">Malnutrition</a> has been a persistent problem in Bangladesh, with the World Bank ranking the country first in the number of malnourished children worldwide.<sup id="cite_ref-248" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-248">[248]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-249" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-249">[249]</a></sup> Twenty-six percent of the population (two-thirds of children under the age of five) are undernourished,<sup id="cite_ref-250" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-250">[250]</a></sup> and 46 percent of children are moderately or severely underweight.<sup id="cite_ref-251" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-251">[251]</a></sup> Forty-three to 60 percent of children under five are smaller than normal; one in five preschool children are vitamin-A deficient, and one in two are anemic.<sup id="cite_ref-252" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-252">[252]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-253" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-253">[253]</a></sup> More than 45 percent of rural families and 76 percent of urban families were below the acceptable caloric-intake level.<sup id="cite_ref-254" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-254">[254]</a></sup></p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Bangladesh" title="Culture of Bangladesh">Culture of Bangladesh</a>, <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Bengal" title="Culture of Bengal">Culture of Bengal</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Bengali_renaissance" title="Bengali renaissance">Bengali renaissance</a></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Visual_arts">Visual arts</span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Bangladeshi_art" title="Bangladeshi art">Bangladeshi art</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Serious_discussion_Du_Fine_Art.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/Serious_discussion_Du_Fine_Art.jpg/220px-Serious_discussion_Du_Fine_Art.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/Serious_discussion_Du_Fine_Art.jpg/330px-Serious_discussion_Du_Fine_Art.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/Serious_discussion_Du_Fine_Art.jpg/440px-Serious_discussion_Du_Fine_Art.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4608" data-file-height="3072" /></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Serious_discussion_Du_Fine_Art.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nA sculpture at the Faculty of Fine Arts, University of Dhaka</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>The recorded history of art in Bangladesh can be traced to the 3rd century BCE, when <a href="/wiki/Terracotta" title="Terracotta">terracotta</a> sculptures were made in the region. In classical antiquity, a notable school of sculptural Hindu, Jain and Buddhist art developed in the Pala Empire and the Sena dynasty. Islamic art evolved since the 14th century. The architecture of the Bengal Sultanate saw a distinct style of domed mosques with complex niche pillars that had no minarets. <a href="/wiki/Mughal_Bengal" class="mw-redirect" title="Mughal Bengal">Mughal Bengal</a>\'s most celebrated artistic tradition was the weaving of <a href="/wiki/Jamdani" title="Jamdani">Jamdani</a> <a href="/wiki/Motif_(textile_arts)" title="Motif (textile arts)">motifs</a> on fine muslin, which is now classified by UNESCO as an <a href="/wiki/Intangible_cultural_heritage" title="Intangible cultural heritage">intangible cultural heritage</a>. Jamdani motifs were similar to Iranian textile art (buta motifs) and Western textile art (<a href="/wiki/Paisley_(design)" title="Paisley (design)">paisley</a>). The Jamdani weavers in Dhaka received imperial patronage.<sup id="cite_ref-255" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-255">[255]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-256" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-256">[256]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Ivory" title="Ivory">Ivory</a> and <a href="/wiki/Brass" title="Brass">brass</a> were also widely used in Mughal art. <a href="/wiki/Pottery" title="Pottery">Pottery</a> is widely used in Bengali culture.</p>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Modern_art" title="Modern art">modern art</a> movement in Bangladesh took shape during the 1950s, particularly with the pioneering works of <a href="/wiki/Zainul_Abedin" title="Zainul Abedin">Zainul Abedin</a>. East Bengal developed its own modernist painting and sculpture traditions, which were distinct from the art movements in West Bengal. The <a href="/wiki/Art_Institute_Dhaka" class="mw-redirect" title="Art Institute Dhaka">Art Institute Dhaka</a> has been an important center for visual art in the region. Its annual <a href="/wiki/Mangal_Shobhajatra" title="Mangal Shobhajatra">Bengali New Year parade</a> was enlisted as an intangible cultural heritage by UNESCO in 2016.</p>\n<p>Modern Bangladesh has produced many of South Asia\'s leading painters, including <a href="/wiki/SM_Sultan" title="SM Sultan">SM Sultan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mohammad_Kibria" title="Mohammad Kibria">Mohammad Kibria</a>, <a href="/wiki/Shahabuddin_Ahmed_(artist)" title="Shahabuddin Ahmed (artist)">Shahabuddin Ahmed</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kanak_Chanpa_Chakma" title="Kanak Chanpa Chakma">Kanak Chanpa Chakma</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kafil_Ahmed" title="Kafil Ahmed">Kafil Ahmed</a>, <a href="/wiki/Saifuddin_Ahmed" title="Saifuddin Ahmed">Saifuddin Ahmed</a>, <a href="/wiki/Qayyum_Chowdhury" title="Qayyum Chowdhury">Qayyum Chowdhury</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rashid_Choudhury" title="Rashid Choudhury">Rashid Choudhury</a>, <a href="/wiki/Quamrul_Hassan" title="Quamrul Hassan">Quamrul Hassan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rafiqun_Nabi" title="Rafiqun Nabi">Rafiqun Nabi</a> and <a href="/wiki/Syed_Jahangir" title="Syed Jahangir">Syed Jahangir</a>, among others. <a href="/wiki/Novera_Ahmed" title="Novera Ahmed">Novera Ahmed</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nitun_Kundu" title="Nitun Kundu">Nitun Kundu</a> were the country\'s pioneers of modernist sculpture.</p>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Chobi_Mela" class="mw-redirect" title="Chobi Mela">Chobi Mela</a> is the largest photography festival in Asia.</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Literature">Literature</span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Bangladeshi_English_literature" title="Bangladeshi English literature">Bangladeshi English literature</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Young_tagore_and_nazrul.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/Young_tagore_and_nazrul.png/220px-Young_tagore_and_nazrul.png" width="220" height="164" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/Young_tagore_and_nazrul.png/330px-Young_tagore_and_nazrul.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/Young_tagore_and_nazrul.png/440px-Young_tagore_and_nazrul.png 2x" data-file-width="782" data-file-height="583" /></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Young_tagore_and_nazrul.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\n<a href="/wiki/Rabindranath_Tagore" title="Rabindranath Tagore">Rabindranath Tagore</a>, author of the <a href="/wiki/National_Anthem_of_Bangladesh" class="mw-redirect" title="National Anthem of Bangladesh">national anthem</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Kazi_Nazrul_Islam" title="Kazi Nazrul Islam">Kazi Nazrul Islam</a>, the <a href="/wiki/National_Poet" class="mw-redirect" title="National Poet">National Poet</a></div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bangla_Academy_Inside_2_by_Ashfaq.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/Bangla_Academy_Inside_2_by_Ashfaq.jpg/220px-Bangla_Academy_Inside_2_by_Ashfaq.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/Bangla_Academy_Inside_2_by_Ashfaq.jpg/330px-Bangla_Academy_Inside_2_by_Ashfaq.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/Bangla_Academy_Inside_2_by_Ashfaq.jpg/440px-Bangla_Academy_Inside_2_by_Ashfaq.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="1535" /></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bangla_Academy_Inside_2_by_Ashfaq.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nThe <a href="/wiki/Bangla_Academy" title="Bangla Academy">Bangla Academy</a></div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>The oldest evidence of writing in Bangladesh is the Mahasthan <a href="/wiki/Brahmi" class="mw-redirect" title="Brahmi">Brahmi</a> Inscription, which dates back to the 3rd century BCE.<sup id="cite_ref-257" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-257">[257]</a></sup> In the Gupta Empire, Sanskrit literature thrived in the region. Bengali developed from <a href="/wiki/Sanskrit" title="Sanskrit">Sanskrit</a> and <a href="/wiki/Magadhi_Prakrit" title="Magadhi Prakrit">Magadhi Prakrit</a> in the 11th century. Bengali literature is a millennium-old tradition; the <a href="/wiki/Charyapada" title="Charyapada">Charyapada</a> are the earliest examples of Bengali poetry. Sufi spiritualism inspired many <a href="/wiki/Bengali_Muslim" class="mw-redirect" title="Bengali Muslim">Bengali Muslim</a> writers. During the Bengal Sultanate, medieval Bengali writers were influenced by <a href="/wiki/Arabic_literature" title="Arabic literature">Arabic</a> and <a href="/wiki/Persian_literature" title="Persian literature">Persian works</a>. <a href="/wiki/Alaol" title="Alaol">Syed Alaol</a> was a noted secular poet and translator. The <a href="/wiki/Chandidas" title="Chandidas">Chandidas</a> are an example of the <a href="/wiki/Bangladeshi_folk_literature" title="Bangladeshi folk literature">Bangladeshi folk literature</a> that developed during the Middle Ages. The Bengal Renaissance shaped the emergence of modern Bengali literature, including novels, short stories and <a href="/wiki/Bengali_science_fiction" title="Bengali science fiction">science fiction</a>. Rabindranath Tagore was the first non-European laureate of the <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Prize_in_Literature" title="Nobel Prize in Literature">Nobel Prize in Literature</a> and is described as the Bengali Shakespeare.<sup id="cite_ref-258" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-258">[258]</a></sup> Kazi Nazrul Islam was a revolutionary poet who espoused spiritual rebellion against colonialism and fascism. Begum Rokeya was a pioneer of <a href="/wiki/Bangladeshi_English_literature" title="Bangladeshi English literature">Bengali writing in English</a>, with her early of work of <a href="/wiki/Feminist_science_fiction" title="Feminist science fiction">feminist science fiction</a>. Other renaissance icons included Michael Madhusudan Dutt and <a href="/wiki/Sarat_Chandra_Chattopadhyay" title="Sarat Chandra Chattopadhyay">Sarat Chandra Chattopadhyay</a>.</p>\n<p>The writer <a href="/wiki/Syed_Mujtaba_Ali" title="Syed Mujtaba Ali">Syed Mujtaba Ali</a> is noted for his cosmopolitan Bengali worldview.<sup id="cite_ref-259" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-259">[259]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Humayun_Ahmed" title="Humayun Ahmed">Humayun Ahmed</a> was a popular writer of modern Bangladeshi <a href="/wiki/Magical_realism" class="mw-redirect" title="Magical realism">magical realism</a> and science fiction. <a href="/wiki/Shamsur_Rahman_(poet)" title="Shamsur Rahman (poet)">Shamsur Rahman</a> was the poet laureate of Bangladesh for many years. <a href="/wiki/Jasimuddin" title="Jasimuddin">Jasimuddin</a> was a renowned pastoral poet. <a href="/wiki/Farrukh_Ahmed" class="mw-redirect" title="Farrukh Ahmed">Farrukh Ahmed</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sufia_Kamal" title="Sufia Kamal">Sufia Kamal</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kaiser_Haq" title="Kaiser Haq">Kaiser Haq</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nirmalendu_Goon" title="Nirmalendu Goon">Nirmalendu Goon</a> are important figures of modern Bangladeshi poetry. Notable writers of Bangladeshi novels include Mir Mosharraf Hossain, <a href="/wiki/Akhteruzzaman_Elias" title="Akhteruzzaman Elias">Akhteruzzaman Elias</a>, <a href="/wiki/Syed_Waliullah" title="Syed Waliullah">Syed Waliullah</a>, <a href="/wiki/Shahidullah_Kaiser" title="Shahidullah Kaiser">Shahidullah Kaiser</a>, <a href="/wiki/Shawkat_Osman" title="Shawkat Osman">Shawkat Osman</a>, <a href="/wiki/Selina_Hossain" title="Selina Hossain">Selina Hossain</a>, <a href="/wiki/Taslima_Nasreen" class="mw-redirect" title="Taslima Nasreen">Taslima Nasreen</a>, <a href="/wiki/Haripada_Datta" title="Haripada Datta">Haripada Datta</a>, <a href="/wiki/Razia_Khan" title="Razia Khan">Razia Khan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Anisul_Hoque" title="Anisul Hoque">Anisul Hoque</a>, <a href="/wiki/Al_Mahmud" title="Al Mahmud">Al Mahmud</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bipradash_Barua" title="Bipradash Barua">Bipradash Barua</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tahmima_Anam" title="Tahmima Anam">Tahmima Anam</a>, <a href="/wiki/Neamat_Imam" title="Neamat Imam">Neamat Imam</a>, <a href="/wiki/Monica_Ali" title="Monica Ali">Monica Ali</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Zia_Haider_Rahman" title="Zia Haider Rahman">Zia Haider Rahman</a>. Many Bangladeshi writers, such as <a href="/wiki/Muhammad_Zafar_Iqbal" class="mw-redirect" title="Muhammad Zafar Iqbal">Muhammad Zafar Iqbal</a>, <a href="/wiki/K._Anis_Ahmed" class="mw-redirect" title="K. Anis Ahmed">K. Anis Ahmed</a> and <a href="/wiki/Farah_Ghuznavi" title="Farah Ghuznavi">Farah Ghuznavi</a> are acclaimed for their short stories.</p>\n<p>The annual <a href="/wiki/Ekushey_Book_Fair" title="Ekushey Book Fair">Ekushey Book Fair</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hay_Festival_Dhaka" class="mw-redirect" title="Hay Festival Dhaka">Dhaka Literature Festival</a>, organized by the <a href="/wiki/Bangla_Academy" title="Bangla Academy">Bangla Academy</a>, are among the largest literary festivals in South Asia.</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Women_in_Bangladesh">Women in Bangladesh</span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Women_in_Bangladesh" title="Women in Bangladesh">Women in Bangladesh</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Irene_Khan_World_Economic_Forum_2007_cropped.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Irene_Khan_World_Economic_Forum_2007_cropped.jpg/170px-Irene_Khan_World_Economic_Forum_2007_cropped.jpg" width="170" height="178" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Irene_Khan_World_Economic_Forum_2007_cropped.jpg/255px-Irene_Khan_World_Economic_Forum_2007_cropped.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Irene_Khan_World_Economic_Forum_2007_cropped.jpg/340px-Irene_Khan_World_Economic_Forum_2007_cropped.jpg 2x" data-file-width="479" data-file-height="501" /></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Irene_Khan_World_Economic_Forum_2007_cropped.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\n<a href="/wiki/Irene_Khan" title="Irene Khan">Irene Khan</a>, the first female Secretary General of <a href="/wiki/Amnesty_International" title="Amnesty International">Amnesty International</a></div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>Although, as of 2015<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Bangladesh&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, several women occupied major political office in Bangladesh, its women continue to live under a patriarchal social regime where violence is common.<sup id="cite_ref-whispers_260-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-whispers-260">[260]</a></sup> Whereas in India and Pakistan women participate less in the workforce as their education increases, the reverse is the case in Bangladesh.<sup id="cite_ref-whispers_260-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-whispers-260">[260]</a></sup></p>\n<p>Bengal has a long history of <a href="/wiki/Feminist_activism" class="mw-redirect" title="Feminist activism">feminist activism</a> dating back to the 19th century. <a href="/wiki/Begum_Rokeya" title="Begum Rokeya">Begum Rokeya</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nawab_Faizunnesa" title="Nawab Faizunnesa">Faizunnessa Chowdhurani</a> played an important role in emancipating Bengali Muslim women from <a href="/wiki/Purdah" title="Purdah">purdah</a>, prior to the country\'s division, as well as promoting girls\' education. Several women were elected to the Bengal Legislative Assembly in the British Raj. The first women\'s magazine, <i><a href="/wiki/Begum_(magazine)" title="Begum (magazine)">Begum</a></i>, was published in 1948.</p>\n<p>In 2008, Bangladeshi female workforce participation stood at 26%.<sup id="cite_ref-261" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-261">[261]</a></sup> Women dominate <a href="/wiki/Blue_collar" class="mw-redirect" title="Blue collar">blue collar</a> jobs in the Bangladeshi garment industry. Agriculture, social services, healthcare and education are also major occupations for Bangladeshi women, while their employment in <a href="/wiki/White-collar_worker" title="White-collar worker">white collar</a> positions has steadily increased.</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Architecture">Architecture</span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Architecture_of_Bangladesh" title="Architecture of Bangladesh">Architecture of Bangladesh</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tleft">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Historical_mosques_in_Bangladesh.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/Historical_mosques_in_Bangladesh.jpg/220px-Historical_mosques_in_Bangladesh.jpg" width="220" height="288" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/Historical_mosques_in_Bangladesh.jpg/330px-Historical_mosques_in_Bangladesh.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/Historical_mosques_in_Bangladesh.jpg/440px-Historical_mosques_in_Bangladesh.jpg 2x" data-file-width="801" data-file-height="1050" /></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Historical_mosques_in_Bangladesh.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nA map showing historical mosques in Bangladesh</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Inside_Kusumba_Mosque_(05).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/Inside_Kusumba_Mosque_%2805%29.jpg/220px-Inside_Kusumba_Mosque_%2805%29.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/Inside_Kusumba_Mosque_%2805%29.jpg/330px-Inside_Kusumba_Mosque_%2805%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/Inside_Kusumba_Mosque_%2805%29.jpg/440px-Inside_Kusumba_Mosque_%2805%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5472" data-file-height="3648" /></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Inside_Kusumba_Mosque_(05).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nThe interior of the black stone <a href="/wiki/Kusumba_Mosque" title="Kusumba Mosque">Kusumba Mosque</a>, one of Bangladesh\'s many acclaimed Sultanate-era mosques.<sup id="cite_ref-262" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-262">[262]</a></sup></div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Sonargaon_by_Rezowan.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/Sonargaon_by_Rezowan.JPG/220px-Sonargaon_by_Rezowan.JPG" width="220" height="124" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/Sonargaon_by_Rezowan.JPG/330px-Sonargaon_by_Rezowan.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/Sonargaon_by_Rezowan.JPG/440px-Sonargaon_by_Rezowan.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3648" data-file-height="2048" /></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Sonargaon_by_Rezowan.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nThe courtyard of a colonial era townhouse in <a href="/wiki/Sonargaon" title="Sonargaon">Sonargaon</a></div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>The architectural traditions of Bangladesh have a 2,500-year-old heritage.<sup id="cite_ref-263" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-263">[263]</a></sup> Terracotta architecture is a distinct feature of Bengal. Pre-Islamic Bengali architecture reached its pinnacle in the Pala Empire, when the Pala School of Sculptural Art established grand structures such as the Somapura Mahavihara. <a href="/wiki/Islamic_architecture" title="Islamic architecture">Islamic architecture</a> began developing under the Bengal Sultanate, when local terracotta styles influenced medieval mosque construction. The Adina Mosque of united Bengal was the largest mosque built on the Indian subcontinent.</p>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Sixty_Dome_Mosque" title="Sixty Dome Mosque">Sixty Dome Mosque</a> was the largest medieval mosque built in Bangladesh, and is a fine example of Turkic-Bengali architecture. The <a href="/wiki/Mughal_architecture" title="Mughal architecture">Mughal style</a> replaced indigenous architecture when Bengal became a province of the Mughal Empire and influenced the development of urban housing. The <a href="/wiki/Kantajew_Temple" title="Kantajew Temple">Kantajew Temple</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dhakeshwari_Temple" title="Dhakeshwari Temple">Dhakeshwari Temple</a> are excellent examples of late medieval <a href="/wiki/Hindu_temple_architecture" title="Hindu temple architecture">Hindu temple architecture</a>. <a href="/wiki/Indo-Saracenic_Revival_architecture" title="Indo-Saracenic Revival architecture">Indo-Saracenic Revival architecture</a>, based on Indo-Islamic styles, flourished during the British period. The zamindar gentry in Bangladesh built numerous Indo-Saracenic palaces and country mansions, such as the <a href="/wiki/Ahsan_Manzil" title="Ahsan Manzil">Ahsan Manzil</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tajhat_Palace" title="Tajhat Palace">Tajhat Palace</a>, <a href="/wiki/Uttara_Gonobhaban" class="mw-redirect" title="Uttara Gonobhaban">Dighapatia Palace</a>, <a href="/wiki/Puthia_Rajbari" title="Puthia Rajbari">Puthia Rajbari</a> and <a href="/wiki/Natore_Rajbari" title="Natore Rajbari">Natore Rajbari</a>.</p>\n<p>Bengali <a href="/wiki/Vernacular_architecture" title="Vernacular architecture">vernacular architecture</a> is noted for pioneering the <a href="/wiki/Bungalow" title="Bungalow">bungalow</a>. Bangladeshi villages consist of <a href="/wiki/Thatch" class="mw-redirect" title="Thatch">thatched</a> roofed houses made of natural materials like <a href="/wiki/Mud" title="Mud">mud</a>, <a href="/wiki/Straw" title="Straw">straw</a>, wood and bamboo. In modern times, village bungalows are increasingly made of <a href="/wiki/Tin" title="Tin">tin</a>.</p>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Muzharul_Islam" title="Muzharul Islam">Muzharul Islam</a> was the pioneer of Bangladeshi modern architecture. His varied works set the course of modern architectural practice in the country. Islam brought leading global architects, including <a href="/wiki/Louis_Kahn" title="Louis Kahn">Louis Kahn</a>, <a href="/wiki/Richard_Neutra" title="Richard Neutra">Richard Neutra</a>, <a href="/wiki/Stanley_Tigerman" title="Stanley Tigerman">Stanley Tigerman</a>, <a href="/wiki/Paul_Rudolph_(architect)" title="Paul Rudolph (architect)">Paul Rudolph</a>, <a href="/wiki/Robert_Boughey" title="Robert Boughey">Robert Boughey</a> and <a href="/wiki/Konstantinos_Apostolos_Doxiadis" class="mw-redirect" title="Konstantinos Apostolos Doxiadis">Konstantinos Doxiadis</a>, to work in erstwhile East Pakistan. Louis Kahn was chosen to design the National Parliament Complex in <a href="/wiki/Sher-e-Bangla_Nagar" class="mw-redirect" title="Sher-e-Bangla Nagar">Sher-e-Bangla Nagar</a>. Kahn\'s monumental designs, combining regional red brick aesthetics, his own concrete and marble <a href="/wiki/Brutalism" class="mw-redirect" title="Brutalism">brutalism</a> and the use of lakes to represent Bengali geography, are regarded as one of the masterpieces of the 20th century. In more recent times, award-winning architects like <a href="/wiki/Rafiq_Azam" title="Rafiq Azam">Rafiq Azam</a> have set the course of contemporary architecture by adopting influences from the works of Islam and Kahn.</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Performing_arts">Performing arts</span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tleft">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Sabina_Yasmin(%E0%A6%B8%E0%A6%BE%E0%A6%AC%E0%A6%BF%E0%A6%A8%E0%A6%BE_%E0%A6%87%E0%A6%AF%E0%A6%BC%E0%A6%BE%E0%A6%B8%E0%A6%AE%E0%A6%BF%E0%A6%A8)_3.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/Sabina_Yasmin%28%E0%A6%B8%E0%A6%BE%E0%A6%AC%E0%A6%BF%E0%A6%A8%E0%A6%BE_%E0%A6%87%E0%A6%AF%E0%A6%BC%E0%A6%BE%E0%A6%B8%E0%A6%AE%E0%A6%BF%E0%A6%A8%29_3.jpg/220px-Sabina_Yasmin%28%E0%A6%B8%E0%A6%BE%E0%A6%AC%E0%A6%BF%E0%A6%A8%E0%A6%BE_%E0%A6%87%E0%A6%AF%E0%A6%BC%E0%A6%BE%E0%A6%B8%E0%A6%AE%E0%A6%BF%E0%A6%A8%29_3.jpg"
