srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/Sabina_Yasmin%28%E0%A6%B8%E0%A6%BE%E0%A6%AC%E0%A6%BF%E0%A6%A8%E0%A6%BE_%E0%A6%87%E0%A6%AF%E0%A6%BC%E0%A6%BE%E0%A6%B8%E0%A6%AE%E0%A6%BF%E0%A6%A8%29_3.jpg/330px-Sabina_Yasmin%28%E0%A6%B8%E0%A6%BE%E0%A6%AC%E0%A6%BF%E0%A6%A8%E0%A6%BE_%E0%A6%87%E0%A6%AF%E0%A6%BC%E0%A6%BE%E0%A6%B8%E0%A6%AE%E0%A6%BF%E0%A6%A8%29_3.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/Sabina_Yasmin%28%E0%A6%B8%E0%A6%BE%E0%A6%AC%E0%A6%BF%E0%A6%A8%E0%A6%BE_%E0%A6%87%E0%A6%AF%E0%A6%BC%E0%A6%BE%E0%A6%B8%E0%A6%AE%E0%A6%BF%E0%A6%A8%29_3.jpg/440px-Sabina_Yasmin%28%E0%A6%B8%E0%A6%BE%E0%A6%AC%E0%A6%BF%E0%A6%A8%E0%A6%BE_%E0%A6%87%E0%A6%AF%E0%A6%BC%E0%A6%BE%E0%A6%B8%E0%A6%AE%E0%A6%BF%E0%A6%A8%29_3.jpg 2x" data-file-width="960" data-file-height="720" /></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Sabina_Yasmin(%E0%A6%B8%E0%A6%BE%E0%A6%AC%E0%A6%BF%E0%A6%A8%E0%A6%BE_%E0%A6%87%E0%A6%AF%E0%A6%BC%E0%A6%BE%E0%A6%B8%E0%A6%AE%E0%A6%BF%E0%A6%A8)_3.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\n<a href="/wiki/Sabina_Yasmin" title="Sabina Yasmin">Sabina Yasmin</a>, a leading Bangladeshi playback singer since the 1970s</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Runa_Laila_in_2017.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/Runa_Laila_in_2017.jpg/220px-Runa_Laila_in_2017.jpg" width="220" height="245" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/Runa_Laila_in_2017.jpg/330px-Runa_Laila_in_2017.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/Runa_Laila_in_2017.jpg/440px-Runa_Laila_in_2017.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2370" data-file-height="2640" /></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Runa_Laila_in_2017.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\n<a href="/wiki/Runa_Laila" title="Runa Laila">Runa Laila</a>, a leading playback singer of South Asia since the 1960s, is based in Bangladesh</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Theatre_in_Bangladesh" title="Theatre in Bangladesh">Theatre in Bangladesh</a> includes various forms with a history dating back to the 4th century CE.<sup id="cite_ref-Ahmed.2C_Syed_Jamil_2000_p._396_264-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ahmed.2C_Syed_Jamil_2000_p._396-264">[264]</a></sup> It includes narrative forms, song and dance forms, supra-personae forms, performances with scroll paintings, puppet theatre and processional forms.<sup id="cite_ref-Ahmed.2C_Syed_Jamil_2000_p._396_264-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ahmed.2C_Syed_Jamil_2000_p._396-264">[264]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Jatra_(theatre)" title="Jatra (theatre)">Jatra</a> is the most popular form of Bengali folk theatre. The dance traditions of Bangladesh include indigenous tribal and Bengali dance forms, as well as <a href="/wiki/Classical_Indian_dance" class="mw-redirect" title="Classical Indian dance">classical Indian dances</a>, including the <a href="/wiki/Kathak" title="Kathak">Kathak</a>, <a href="/wiki/Odissi" title="Odissi">Odissi</a> and <a href="/wiki/Manipuri_dance" title="Manipuri dance">Manipuri dances</a>.</p>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Music_of_Bangladesh" title="Music of Bangladesh">music of Bangladesh</a> features the Baul mystical tradition, listed by UNESCO as a <a href="/wiki/Masterpiece_of_the_Oral_and_Intangible_Heritage_of_Humanity" class="mw-redirect" title="Masterpiece of the Oral and Intangible Heritage of Humanity">Masterpiece of Intangible Cultural Heritage</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-265" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-265">[265]</a></sup> Numerous lyric-based musical traditions, varying from one region to the next, exist, including <a href="/wiki/Gombhira" title="Gombhira">Gombhira</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bhatiali" title="Bhatiali">Bhatiali</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bhawaiya" title="Bhawaiya">Bhawaiya</a>. Folk music is accompanied by a one-stringed instrument known as the <a href="/wiki/Ektara" title="Ektara">ektara</a>. Other instruments include the <a href="/wiki/Dotara" title="Dotara">dotara</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dhol" title="Dhol">dhol</a>, flute, and <a href="/wiki/Tabla" title="Tabla">tabla</a>. Bengali classical music includes <a href="/wiki/Tagore_songs" class="mw-redirect" title="Tagore songs">Tagore songs</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nazrul_geeti" class="mw-redirect" title="Nazrul geeti">Nazrul geeti</a>. Bangladesh has a rich tradition of <a href="/wiki/Indian_classical_music" title="Indian classical music">Indian classical music</a>, which uses instruments like the <a href="/wiki/Sitar" title="Sitar">sitar</a>, tabla, <a href="/wiki/Sarod" title="Sarod">sarod</a> and <a href="/wiki/Santoor" title="Santoor">santoor</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-266" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-266">[266]</a></sup></p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Martial_arts">Martial arts</span></h3>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Bangladeshi_martial_arts" title="Bangladeshi martial arts">Bangladeshi martial arts</a> evolved in villages where zamindars employed large private armies to protect their landholdings. The <a href="/wiki/Lathi_khela" title="Lathi khela">Lathi khela</a> and <a href="/wiki/Boli_Khela" title="Boli Khela">Boli Khela</a> are two major forms of Bengali martial arts.</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Country_boats">Country boats</span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Country_boats_in_Bangladesh" title="Country boats in Bangladesh">Country boats in Bangladesh</a></div>\n<p>There are 150 different types of boats and canoes in Bangladesh.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> The timber used in boat-making is from local woods such as Jarul (dipterocarpus turbinatus), sal (shorea robusta), sundari (heritiera fomes) and Myanmar teak (tectons grandis). The region was renowned for shipbuilding during the medieval period, when its shipyards catered to major powers in Eurasia, including the Mughals and the Ottomans.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Textiles">Textiles</span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Textile_arts_of_Bangladesh" title="Textile arts of Bangladesh">Textile arts of Bangladesh</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Kantha_(Quilt)_LACMA_AC1994.131.1.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Kantha_%28Quilt%29_LACMA_AC1994.131.1.jpg/220px-Kantha_%28Quilt%29_LACMA_AC1994.131.1.jpg" width="220" height="162" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Kantha_%28Quilt%29_LACMA_AC1994.131.1.jpg/330px-Kantha_%28Quilt%29_LACMA_AC1994.131.1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Kantha_%28Quilt%29_LACMA_AC1994.131.1.jpg/440px-Kantha_%28Quilt%29_LACMA_AC1994.131.1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2100" data-file-height="1548" /></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Kantha_(Quilt)_LACMA_AC1994.131.1.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\n19th century <a href="/wiki/Nakshi_kantha" title="Nakshi kantha">Nakshi kantha</a></div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Nakshi_Kantha" class="mw-redirect" title="Nakshi Kantha">Nakshi Kantha</a> is a centuries-old <a href="/wiki/Embroidery" title="Embroidery">embroidery</a> tradition for <a href="/wiki/Quilt" title="Quilt">quilts</a>, said to be indigenous to eastern Bengal (i.e. Bangladesh). The sari is the national dress for Bangladeshi women. Mughal Dhaka was renowned for producing the finest muslin saris, including the famed <a href="/wiki/Dhakai" title="Dhakai">Dhakai</a> and Jamdani, the weaving of which is listed by UNESCO as one of the masterpieces of humanity\'s intangible cultural heritage.<sup id="cite_ref-267" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-267">[267]</a></sup> Bangladesh also produces the <a href="/wiki/Rajshahi_silk" title="Rajshahi silk">Rajshahi silk</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Shalwar_kameez" title="Shalwar kameez">shalwar kameez</a> is also widely worn by Bangladeshi women. In urban areas some women can be seen in western clothing. The <a href="/wiki/Kurta" title="Kurta">kurta</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sherwani" title="Sherwani">sherwani</a> are the national dress of Bangladeshi men; the <a href="/wiki/Lungi" title="Lungi">lungi</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dhoti" title="Dhoti">dhoti</a> are worn by them in informal settings. Aside from ethnic wear, domestically <a href="/wiki/Tailored" class="mw-redirect" title="Tailored">tailored</a> <a href="/wiki/Suit_(clothing)" title="Suit (clothing)">suits</a> and <a href="/wiki/Neckties" class="mw-redirect" title="Neckties">neckties</a> are customarily worn by the country\'s men in offices, in schools and at social events.</p>\n<p>The handloom industry supplies 60\xe2\x80\x9365% of the country\'s clothing demand.<sup id="cite_ref-268" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-268">[268]</a></sup> The Bengali ethnic <a href="/wiki/Fashion_industry" class="mw-redirect" title="Fashion industry">fashion industry</a> has flourished in the changing environment of the fashion world. The retailer <a href="/wiki/Aarong" title="Aarong">Aarong</a> is one of the most successful ethnic wear brands in South Asia. The development of the Bangladesh textile industry, which supplies leading international brands, has promoted the production and retail of modern Western attire locally, with the country now having a number of expanding local brands like Westecs and Yellow. Bangladesh is the world\'s second largest garments exporter.</p>\n<p>Among Bangladesh\'s fashion designers, <a href="/wiki/Bibi_Russell" title="Bibi Russell">Bibi Russell</a> has received international acclaim for her "Fashion for Development" shows.<sup id="cite_ref-269" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-269">[269]</a></sup></p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cuisine">Cuisine</span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Bengali_cuisine" title="Bengali cuisine">Bengali cuisine</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bangladeshi_cuisine" title="Bangladeshi cuisine">Bangladeshi cuisine</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:The_Surma_-_geograph.org.uk_-_242294.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/The_Surma_-_geograph.org.uk_-_242294.jpg/220px-The_Surma_-_geograph.org.uk_-_242294.jpg" width="220" height="306" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/The_Surma_-_geograph.org.uk_-_242294.jpg/330px-The_Surma_-_geograph.org.uk_-_242294.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/The_Surma_-_geograph.org.uk_-_242294.jpg/440px-The_Surma_-_geograph.org.uk_-_242294.jpg 2x" data-file-width="460" data-file-height="640" /></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:The_Surma_-_geograph.org.uk_-_242294.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nThe majority of restaurants offering <a href="/wiki/South_Asian_cuisine" title="South Asian cuisine">South Asian cuisine</a> in Britain are owned by British Bangladeshis. Pictured here is a restaurant in London named after the <a href="/wiki/Surma_River" title="Surma River">Surma River</a> of northeastern Bangladesh</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p><a href="/wiki/White_rice" title="White rice">White rice</a> is the staple of Bangladeshi cuisine, along with many vegetables and <a href="/wiki/Lentil" title="Lentil">lentils</a>. Rice preparations also include Bengali <a href="/wiki/Biryani" title="Biryani">biryanis</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pilaf" title="Pilaf">pulaos</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Khichuri" class="mw-redirect" title="Khichuri">khichuris</a>. <a href="/wiki/Mustard_(condiment)" title="Mustard (condiment)">Mustard</a> sauce, <a href="/wiki/Ghee" title="Ghee">ghee</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sunflower_oil" title="Sunflower oil">sunflower oil</a> and fruit <a href="/wiki/Chutney" title="Chutney">chutneys</a> are widely used in Bangladeshi cooking. Fish is the main source of protein in Bengali cuisine. The <a href="/wiki/Hilsa" class="mw-redirect" title="Hilsa">Hilsa</a> is the national fish and immensely popular across Bangladesh. Other kinds of fish eaten include <a href="/wiki/Rohu" title="Rohu">rohu</a>, <a href="/wiki/Butterfish" class="mw-redirect" title="Butterfish">butterfish</a>, catfish, <a href="/wiki/Tilapia" title="Tilapia">tilapia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Barramundi" title="Barramundi">barramundi</a>. <a href="/wiki/Fish_egg" class="mw-redirect" title="Fish egg">Fish eggs</a> are a gourmet delicacy. Seafood holds an important place in Bengali cuisine, especially <a href="/wiki/Lobster" title="Lobster">lobsters</a>, <a href="/wiki/Shrimp" title="Shrimp">shrimps</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dried_fish" title="Dried fish">dried fish</a>. Meat consumption includes chicken, beef, <a href="/wiki/Mutton" class="mw-redirect" title="Mutton">mutton</a>, <a href="/wiki/Venison" title="Venison">venison</a>, <a href="/wiki/Duck" title="Duck">duck</a> and <a href="/wiki/Squab_(food)" class="mw-redirect" title="Squab (food)">squab</a>. In Chittagong, <i>Mezban</i> feasts are a popular tradition featuring the serving of hot beef <a href="/wiki/Curry" title="Curry">curry</a>. In Sylhet, the <i><a href="/wiki/Shatkora" class="mw-redirect" title="Shatkora">shatkora</a></i> lemons are used to marinate dishes. In the tribal Hill Tracts, bamboo shoot cooking is prevalent. Bangladesh has a vast spread of desserts, including distinctive <a href="/wiki/Sweets" class="mw-redirect" title="Sweets">sweets</a> like <i><a href="/wiki/Rasgulla" title="Rasgulla">R\xc3\xb4shogolla</a></i>, <i>R\xc3\xb4shomalai</i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Chomchom" title="Chomchom">Chomchom</a></i>, <i>Mishti Doi</i> and <i>Kalojaam</i>. <a href="/wiki/Pitha" title="Pitha">Pithas</a> are traditional boiled desserts made with rice or fruits. <a href="/wiki/Halwa" class="mw-redirect" title="Halwa">Halwa</a> is served during religious festivities. <a href="/wiki/Naan" title="Naan">Naan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Paratha" title="Paratha">paratha</a>, <a href="/wiki/Luchi" title="Luchi">luchi</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bakarkhani" title="Bakarkhani">bakarkhani</a> are the main local breads. <a href="/wiki/Black_tea" title="Black tea">Black tea</a> is offered to guests as a gesture of welcome. <a href="/wiki/Kebab" title="Kebab">Kebabs</a> are widely popular across Bangladesh, particularly <a href="/wiki/Seekh_kebab" class="mw-redirect" title="Seekh kebab">seekh kebabs</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chicken_tikka" title="Chicken tikka">chicken tikka</a> and <a href="/wiki/Shashlik" title="Shashlik">shashliks</a>.</p>\n<p>Bangladesh shares its culinary heritage with the neighboring Indian state of <a href="/wiki/West_Bengal" title="West Bengal">West Bengal</a>. The two regions have several differences, however. In Muslim-majority Bangladesh, meat consumption is greater; whereas in Hindu-majority West Bengal, vegetarianism is more prevalent. The Bangladeshi diaspora dominates the South Asian restaurant industry in many Western countries, particularly in the United Kingdom.</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Festivals">Festivals</span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Public_holidays_in_Bangladesh" title="Public holidays in Bangladesh">Public holidays in Bangladesh</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tleft">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:272px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Mangal_Shobhajatra_in_Dhaka.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Mangal_Shobhajatra_in_Dhaka.jpg/270px-Mangal_Shobhajatra_in_Dhaka.jpg" width="270" height="179" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Mangal_Shobhajatra_in_Dhaka.jpg/405px-Mangal_Shobhajatra_in_Dhaka.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Mangal_Shobhajatra_in_Dhaka.jpg/540px-Mangal_Shobhajatra_in_Dhaka.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3264" data-file-height="2161" /></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Mangal_Shobhajatra_in_Dhaka.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nThe annual <a href="/wiki/Bengali_New_Year" class="mw-redirect" title="Bengali New Year">Bengali New Year</a> parade</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p><i><a href="/wiki/Pohela_Boishakh" class="mw-redirect" title="Pohela Boishakh">Pohela Boishakh</a></i>, the Bengali new year, is the major festival of <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Bengal" title="Culture of Bengal">Bengali culture</a> and sees widespread festivities. Of the major holidays celebrated in Bangladesh, only Pohela Boishakh comes without any preexisting expectations (specific religious identity, culture of gift-giving, etc.). Unlike holidays like <a href="/wiki/Eid_al-Fitr" title="Eid al-Fitr">Eid al-Fitr</a>, where dressing up in lavish clothes has become a norm, or <a href="/wiki/Christmas" title="Christmas">Christmas</a> where exchanging gifts has become an integral part of the holiday, Pohela Boishakh is really about celebrating the simpler, rural roots of the Bengal. As a result, more people can participate in the festivities together without the burden of having to reveal one\'s class, religion, or financial capacity. Other cultural festivals include <a href="/wiki/Nabanna" title="Nabanna">Nabonno</a>, and Poush Parbon both of which are Bengali harvest festivals.</p>\n<p>The Muslim festivals of Eid al-Fitr, <a href="/wiki/Eid_al-Adha" title="Eid al-Adha">Eid al-Adha</a>, <a href="/wiki/Milad_un_Nabi" class="mw-redirect" title="Milad un Nabi">Milad un Nabi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Muharram" title="Muharram">Muharram</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chand_Raat" class="mw-redirect" title="Chand Raat">Chand Raat</a>, <a href="/wiki/Barat_Night" class="mw-redirect" title="Barat Night">Shab-e-Barat</a>; the Hindu festivals of <a href="/wiki/Durga_Puja" title="Durga Puja">Durga Puja</a>, <a href="/wiki/Janmashtami" class="mw-redirect" title="Janmashtami">Janmashtami</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rath_Yatra" class="mw-redirect" title="Rath Yatra">Rath Yatra</a>; the Buddhist festival of <a href="/wiki/Vesak" title="Vesak">Buddha Purnima</a>, which marks the birth of <a href="/wiki/Gautama_Buddha" title="Gautama Buddha">Gautama Buddha</a>, and Christian festival of Christmas are <a href="/wiki/Public_holidays_in_Bangladesh" title="Public holidays in Bangladesh">national holidays</a> in Bangladesh and see the most widespread celebrations in the country.</p>\n<p>Alongside are national days like the remembrance of 21 February 1952 <a href="/wiki/Language_Movement_Day" title="Language Movement Day">Language Movement Day</a> (<a href="/wiki/International_Mother_Language_Day" title="International Mother Language Day">International Mother Language Day</a>), <a href="/wiki/Independence_Day_(Bangladesh)" title="Independence Day (Bangladesh)">Independence Day</a> and <a href="/wiki/Victory_day_of_Bangladesh" title="Victory day of Bangladesh">Victory Day</a>. On Language Movement Day, people congregate at the <a href="/wiki/Shaheed_Minar,_Dhaka" title="Shaheed Minar, Dhaka">Shaheed Minar</a> in Dhaka to remember the national heroes of the Bengali Language Movement, and at the <a href="/wiki/Jatiyo_Smriti_Soudho" class="mw-redirect" title="Jatiyo Smriti Soudho">Jatiyo Smriti Soudho</a> on Independence Day and Victory Day to remember the national heroes of the Bangladesh Liberation War. These occasions are observed with public ceremonies, parades, rallies by citizens, political speeches, fairs, concerts, and various other public and private events, celebrating the history and traditions of Bangladesh. TV and radio stations broadcast special programs and patriotic songs, and many schools and colleges organise fairs, festivals, and concerts that draw the participation of citizens from all levels of Bangladeshi society.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">Sports</span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Sports_in_Bangladesh" class="mw-redirect" title="Sports in Bangladesh">Sports in Bangladesh</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:272px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bangladesh_Players_Celebrate_Fall_of_Wicket.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/Bangladesh_Players_Celebrate_Fall_of_Wicket.jpg/270px-Bangladesh_Players_Celebrate_Fall_of_Wicket.jpg" width="270" height="157" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/Bangladesh_Players_Celebrate_Fall_of_Wicket.jpg/405px-Bangladesh_Players_Celebrate_Fall_of_Wicket.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/Bangladesh_Players_Celebrate_Fall_of_Wicket.jpg/540px-Bangladesh_Players_Celebrate_Fall_of_Wicket.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1459" data-file-height="848" /></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bangladesh_Players_Celebrate_Fall_of_Wicket.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nThe <a href="/wiki/Bangladesh_cricket_team" class="mw-redirect" title="Bangladesh cricket team">Bangladesh cricket team</a> celebrating the fall of a wicket against Zimbabwe</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Cricket" title="Cricket">Cricket</a> is one of the most popular sports in Bangladesh, followed by <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">football</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Bangladesh_national_cricket_team" title="Bangladesh national cricket team">national cricket team</a> participated in their first <a href="/wiki/Cricket_World_Cup" title="Cricket World Cup">Cricket World Cup</a> in 1999, and the following year was granted elite <a href="/wiki/Test_cricket" title="Test cricket">Test cricket</a> status. They have however struggled, recording only ten test match victories: one against <a href="/wiki/Australia" title="Australia">Australia</a>, one against <a href="/wiki/England" title="England">England</a>, one against <a href="/wiki/Sri_Lanka" title="Sri Lanka">Sri Lanka</a> in Sri Lanka, five against <a href="/wiki/Zimbabwe" title="Zimbabwe">Zimbabwe</a> (one in 2005, one in 2013 in Zimbabwe, and three in 2014), two in a 2\xe2\x80\x930 series victory over the <a href="/wiki/West_Indies" title="West Indies">West Indies</a> in the West Indies in 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-270" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-270">[270]</a></sup> Six of Bangladesh\'s ten test match victories came in between 2014 and 2017.</p>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Rani_Hamid_Photo.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/Rani_Hamid_Photo.JPG/220px-Rani_Hamid_Photo.JPG" width="220" height="222" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/Rani_Hamid_Photo.JPG/330px-Rani_Hamid_Photo.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/Rani_Hamid_Photo.JPG/440px-Rani_Hamid_Photo.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1278" data-file-height="1290" /></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Rani_Hamid_Photo.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\n<a href="/wiki/Rani_Hamid" title="Rani Hamid">Rani Hamid</a> became Bangladesh\'s first <a href="/wiki/Woman_International_Master" class="mw-redirect" title="Woman International Master">Woman International Master</a> in <a href="/wiki/Chess" title="Chess">chess</a> in 1985</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>The team has been more successful in <a href="/wiki/One_Day_International_cricket" class="mw-redirect" title="One Day International cricket">One Day International cricket</a> (ODI). They reached the quarter-final of the <a href="/wiki/2015_Cricket_World_Cup" title="2015 Cricket World Cup">2015 Cricket World Cup</a>. They also reached the semi-final of the <a href="/wiki/2017_ICC_Champions_Trophy" title="2017 ICC Champions Trophy">2017 ICC Champions Trophy</a>. They whitewashed <a href="/wiki/Pakistan" title="Pakistan">Pakistan</a> in a home ODI series in 2015 followed by home ODI series wins against <a href="/wiki/India" title="India">India</a> and <a href="/wiki/South_Africa" title="South Africa">South Africa</a>. They also won home ODI series by 4\xe2\x80\x930 in 2010 against <a href="/wiki/New_Zealand" title="New Zealand">New Zealand</a> and whitewashed them in the home ODI series in 2013. In July 2010, they celebrated their first-ever win over England in England. In late 2012, they won a five-match home ODI series 3-2 against a full-strength West Indies National team. In 2011, Bangladesh successfully co-hosted the <a href="/wiki/ICC_Cricket_World_Cup_2011" class="mw-redirect" title="ICC Cricket World Cup 2011">ICC Cricket World Cup 2011</a> with India and Sri Lanka. They also hosted the <a href="/wiki/2014_ICC_World_Twenty20" title="2014 ICC World Twenty20">2014 ICC World Twenty20</a> championship. Bangladesh hosted the <a href="/wiki/Asia_Cup" title="Asia Cup">Asia Cup</a> on four occasions in 2000, 2012, 2014, and 2016. In <a href="/wiki/2012_Asia_Cup" title="2012 Asia Cup">2012 Asia Cup</a>, Bangladesh beat India and Sri Lanka but lost the final game against Pakistan. However, it was the first time Bangladesh had advanced to the final of any top-class international cricket tournament. They reached the final again at the <a href="/wiki/2016_Asia_Cup" title="2016 Asia Cup">2016 Asia Cup</a>. They participated at the <a href="/wiki/2010_Asian_Games" title="2010 Asian Games">2010 Asian Games</a> in Guangzhou, defeating Afghanistan to claim their Gold Medal in the first-ever cricket tournament held in the Asian Games. Bangladeshi cricketer <a href="/wiki/Sakib_Al_Hasan" class="mw-redirect" title="Sakib Al Hasan">Sakib Al Hasan</a> is No.1 on the <a href="/wiki/International_Cricket_Council" title="International Cricket Council">ICC\'s</a> <a href="/wiki/All-rounder" title="All-rounder">all-rounder</a> rankings in all three formats of the cricket.<sup id="cite_ref-271" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-271">[271]</a></sup></p>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Kabaddi" title="Kabaddi">Kabaddi</a> \xe2\x80\x93 very popular in Bangladesh \xe2\x80\x93 is the national game.<sup id="cite_ref-272" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-272">[272]</a></sup> Other popular sports include <a href="/wiki/Field_hockey" title="Field hockey">field hockey</a>, tennis, badminton, <a href="/wiki/Team_handball" class="mw-redirect" title="Team handball">handball</a>, basketball, volleyball, chess, <a href="/wiki/Shooting_sports" title="Shooting sports">shooting</a>, <a href="/wiki/Angling" title="Angling">angling</a>. The <a href="/wiki/National_Sports_Council" title="National Sports Council">National Sports Council</a> regulates 42 different sporting federations.<sup id="cite_ref-273" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-273">[273]</a></sup></p>\n<p>Bangladesh has five grandmasters in chess. Among them, <a href="/wiki/Niaz_Murshed" title="Niaz Murshed">Niaz Murshed</a> was the first grandmaster in South Asia. In another achievement, <a href="/wiki/Margarita_Mamun" title="Margarita Mamun">Margarita Mamun</a>, a Russian <a href="/wiki/Rhythmic_gymnast" class="mw-redirect" title="Rhythmic gymnast">rhythmic gymnast</a> of Bangladeshi origin, won gold medal in <a href="/wiki/2016_Summer_Olympics" title="2016 Summer Olympics">2016 Summer Olympics</a> and became world champion in 2013 and 2014.</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Media_and_cinema">Media and cinema</span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Media_of_Bangladesh" title="Media of Bangladesh">Media of Bangladesh</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cinema_of_Bangladesh" title="Cinema of Bangladesh">Cinema of Bangladesh</a></div>\n<p>The Bangladeshi press is diverse, outspoken and privately owned. Over 200 newspapers are published in the country. <a href="/wiki/Bangladesh_Betar" title="Bangladesh Betar">Bangladesh Betar</a> is the state-run radio service.<sup id="cite_ref-274" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-274">[274]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/British_Broadcasting_Corporation" class="mw-redirect" title="British Broadcasting Corporation">British Broadcasting Corporation</a> operates the popular <a href="/wiki/BBC_Bangla" title="BBC Bangla">BBC Bangla</a> news and current affairs service. Bengali broadcasts from <a href="/wiki/Voice_of_America" title="Voice of America">Voice of America</a> are also very popular. <a href="/wiki/Bangladesh_Television" title="Bangladesh Television">Bangladesh Television</a> (BTV) is the state-owned television network. There more than 20 privately owned television networks, including several <a href="/wiki/News_channel" class="mw-redirect" title="News channel">news channels</a>. <a href="/wiki/Freedom_of_the_media" class="mw-redirect" title="Freedom of the media">Freedom of the media</a> remains a major concern, due to government attempts at censorship and the harassment of journalists.</p>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Cinema_of_Bangladesh" title="Cinema of Bangladesh">cinema of Bangladesh</a> dates back to 1898, when films began screening at the Crown Theatre in Dhaka. The first bioscope on the subcontinent was established in Dhaka that year. The <a href="/wiki/Dhaka_Nawab_Family" class="mw-redirect" title="Dhaka Nawab Family">Dhaka Nawab Family</a> patronized the production of several <a href="/wiki/Silent_film" title="Silent film">silent films</a> in the 1920s and 30s. In 1931, the East Bengal Cinematograph Society released the first full-length feature film in Bangladesh, titled the <i>Last Kiss</i>. The first feature film in East Pakistan, <i><a href="/wiki/Mukh_O_Mukhosh" title="Mukh O Mukhosh">Mukh O Mukhosh</a></i>, was released in 1956. During the 1960s, 25\xe2\x80\x9330 films were produced annually in Dhaka. By the 2000s, Bangladesh produced 80\xe2\x80\x93100 films a year. While the Bangladeshi film industry has achieved limited commercial success, the country has produced notable independent filmmakers. <a href="/wiki/Zahir_Raihan" title="Zahir Raihan">Zahir Raihan</a> was a prominent documentary-maker who was assassinated in 1971. The late <a href="/wiki/Tareque_Masud" title="Tareque Masud">Tareque Masud</a> is regarded as one of Bangladesh\'s outstanding directors due to his numerous productions on historical and social issues. Masud was honored by <a href="/wiki/FIPRESCI" class="mw-redirect" title="FIPRESCI">FIPRESCI</a> at the 2002 <a href="/wiki/Cannes_Film_Festival" title="Cannes Film Festival">Cannes Film Festival</a> for his film <i><a href="/wiki/Matir_Moina" title="Matir Moina">The Clay Bird</a></i>. <a href="/wiki/Tanvir_Mokammel" title="Tanvir Mokammel">Tanvir Mokammel</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mostofa_Sarwar_Farooki" title="Mostofa Sarwar Farooki">Mostofa Sarwar Farooki</a>, Humayun Ahmed, <a href="/wiki/Alamgir_Kabir_(film_maker)" title="Alamgir Kabir (film maker)">Alamgir Kabir</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Chashi_Nazrul_Islam" title="Chashi Nazrul Islam">Chashi Nazrul Islam</a> are some of the prominent directors of Bangladeshi cinema.</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Rickshaws">Rickshaws</span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Rickshaw_art_in_Bangladesh" title="Rickshaw art in Bangladesh">Rickshaw art in Bangladesh</a></div>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Cycle_rickshaw" title="Cycle rickshaw">Cycle rickshaws</a> are the most popular form of public transport in Bangladesh. Dhaka, the nation\'s biggest city, is nicknamed the <i>Rickshaw Capital of the World</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-bbc.com_275-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbc.com-275">[275]</a></sup> Rickshaws also ply the streets of other major cities, as well as the countryside. Bangladeshi rickshaws are decorated with colorful posters and boards, often depicting movie stars, national monuments or religious icons. <a href="/wiki/Rickshaw_art" title="Rickshaw art">Rickshaw art</a> is considered a form of <a href="/wiki/Neo-romanticism" title="Neo-romanticism">neo-romanticism</a>. This unique trend started in Rajshahi and Dhaka in the 1950s. Each region of Bangladesh has a distinct style of rickshaw art. For example, rickshaw art in Chittagong and Comilla are dominated by floral scenery and Arabic texts. Auto-rickshaws are widely seen in urban centers. Cycle-driven carts are found in many parts of the country. Bangladeshi rickshaw art has received international fame, and has been called "people\'s art".</p>\n<p>Rickshaw driving provides employment for many poor Bangladeshis coming from rural areas.<sup id="cite_ref-276" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-276">[276]</a></sup></p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Museums_and_libraries">Museums and libraries</span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Museums_in_Bangladesh" class="mw-redirect" title="Museums in Bangladesh">Museums in Bangladesh</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_libraries_in_Bangladesh" title="List of libraries in Bangladesh">List of libraries in Bangladesh</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Tajhat_Palace_232.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/Tajhat_Palace_232.JPG/220px-Tajhat_Palace_232.JPG" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/Tajhat_Palace_232.JPG/330px-Tajhat_Palace_232.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/Tajhat_Palace_232.JPG/440px-Tajhat_Palace_232.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1280" data-file-height="960" /></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Tajhat_Palace_232.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nThe <a href="/wiki/Tajhat_Palace" title="Tajhat Palace">Tajhat Palace Museum</a> in <a href="/wiki/Rangpur_City" title="Rangpur City">Rangpur</a></div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Northbrook_Hall_05.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/Northbrook_Hall_05.JPG/220px-Northbrook_Hall_05.JPG" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/Northbrook_Hall_05.JPG/330px-Northbrook_Hall_05.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/Northbrook_Hall_05.JPG/440px-Northbrook_Hall_05.JPG 2x" data-file-width="4928" data-file-height="3264" /></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Northbrook_Hall_05.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\n<a href="/wiki/Northbrook_Hall" title="Northbrook Hall">Northbrook Hall</a>, a public library opened in 1882 with rare book collections from the <a href="/wiki/British_Raj" title="British Raj">British Raj</a><sup id="cite_ref-277" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-277">[277]</a></sup></div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Varendra_Research_Museum" title="Varendra Research Museum">Varendra Research Museum</a> is the oldest museum in Bangladesh. It houses important collections from both the pre-Islamic and Islamic periods, including the sculptures of the Pala-Sena School of Art and the Indus Valley Civilization; as well as Sanskrit, Arabic and Persian manuscripts and inscriptions. The Ahsan Manzil, the former residence of the Nawab of Dhaka, is a national museum housing collections from the British Raj. It was the site of the founding conference of the All India Muslim League and hosted many British Viceroys in Dhaka.</p>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Tajhat_Palace" title="Tajhat Palace">Tajhat</a> Palace Museum preserves artifacts of the rich cultural heritage of North Bengal, including Hindu-Buddhist sculptures and Islamic manuscripts. The <a href="/wiki/Mymensingh_Museum" title="Mymensingh Museum">Mymensingh Museum</a> houses the personal antique collections of Bengali aristocrats in central Bengal. The <a href="/wiki/Ethnological_Museum_of_Chittagong" class="mw-redirect" title="Ethnological Museum of Chittagong">Ethnological Museum of Chittagong</a> showcases the lifestyle of various tribes in Bangladesh. The <a href="/wiki/Bangladesh_National_Museum" title="Bangladesh National Museum">Bangladesh National Museum</a> is located in <a href="/wiki/Ramna" class="mw-redirect" title="Ramna">Ramna</a>, Dhaka and has a rich collection of antiquities. The <a href="/wiki/Liberation_War_Museum" title="Liberation War Museum">Liberation War Museum</a> documents the Bangladeshi struggle for independence and the 1971 genocide.</p>\n<p>In ancient times, manuscripts were written on palm leaves, tree barks, parchment vellum and terracotta plates and preserved at monasteries known as <i><a href="/wiki/Vihara" title="Vihara">viharas</a></i>. The Hussain Shahi dynasty established royal libraries during the Bengal Sultanate. Libraries were established in each district of Bengal by the zamindar gentry during the Bengal Renaissance in the 19th-century. The trend of establishing libraries continued until the beginning of World War II. In 1854, four major public libraries were opened, including the Bogra Woodburn Library, the Rangpur Public Library, the Jessore Institute Public Library and the Barisal Public Library.</p>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Northbrook_Hall" title="Northbrook Hall">Northbrook Hall Public Library</a> was established in Dhaka in 1882 in honour of <a href="/wiki/Lord_Northbrook" class="mw-redirect" title="Lord Northbrook">Lord Northbrook</a>, the Governor-General. Other libraries established in the British period included the Victoria Public Library, Natore (1901), the Sirajganj Public Library (1882), the Rajshahi Public Library (1884), the Comilla Birchandra Library (1885), the Shah Makhdum Institute Public Library, Rajshahi (1891), the Noakhali Town Hall Public Library (1896), the Prize Memorial Library, Sylhet (1897), the Chittagong Municipality Public Library (1904) and the Varendra Research Library (1910). The Great Bengal Library Association was formed in 1925.<sup id="cite_ref-278" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-278">[278]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Central_Public_Library_(Dhaka)" title="Central Public Library (Dhaka)">Central Public Library of Dhaka</a> was established in 1959. The <a href="/wiki/National_Library_of_Bangladesh" title="National Library of Bangladesh">National Library of Bangladesh</a> was established in 1972. The <a href="/wiki/Bishwo_Shahitto_Kendro" title="Bishwo Shahitto Kendro">World Literature Center</a>, founded by <a href="/wiki/Ramon_Magsaysay_Award" title="Ramon Magsaysay Award">Ramon Magsaysay Award</a> winner <a href="/wiki/Abdullah_Abu_Sayeed" title="Abdullah Abu Sayeed">Abdullah Abu Sayeed</a>, is noted for operating numerous <a href="/wiki/Mobile_library" class="mw-redirect" title="Mobile library">mobile libraries</a> across Bangladesh and was awarded the UNESCO Jon Amos Comenius Medal.</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span></h2>\n<table To the extent that there is evidence that the womenfolk donated their own bangles and gold ornaments, and the funds were used for the establishment of a bank, the construction of the parliament building and the purchase of armaments and ammunitions to help the war of liberation.
